## **PART I** 

## **Item 1. Business** 

Oracle provides products and services that address enterprise informaïŋ―on technology (IT) environments. Our products and services include enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings that are delivered worldwide through a variety of flexible and interoperable IT deployment models. These models include on-premise, cloud-based and hybrid deployments (an approach that combines both on-premise and cloud-based deployments), such as Oracle Exadata Cloud@Customer and Dedicated Region offerings (instances of Oracle Cloud in a customerâs own data center) and mulïŋ―cloud opïŋ―ons that enable customers to use Oracle Cloud in conjuncïŋ―on with other public clouds. Accordingly, we offer choice and flexibility to our customers and facilitate the product, service and deployment combinaïŋ―ons that best suit our customersâ needs. Our customers include businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and resellers that we market and sell to directly through our worldwide sales force and indirectly through the Oracle Partner Network. Using Oracle technologies, our customers build, deploy, run, manage and support their internal and external products, services and business operaïŋ―ons, including, for example, a global cloud applicaïŋ―ons developer that uïŋ―lizes Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (OCI) to power its soïŋ―ware-as-a-service (SaaS) offerings; a mulïŋ―naïŋ―onal financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―on that runs its banking applicaïŋ―ons using Oracle Exadata Cloud@Customer; and a global consumer products company that leverages Oracle Fusion Cloud Enterprise Resource Planning for its accounïŋ―ng processes, risk management, supply chain and financial planning funcïŋ―ons. 

Oracle SaaS and OCI (collecïŋ―vely Oracle Cloud Services) offerings provide comprehensive and integrated applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure services delivered via various cloud delivery models enabling our customers to choose the best opïŋ―on that meets their specific business needs. Oracle Cloud Services integrate the IT components, including soïŋ―ware, hardware and services, on a customerâs behalf in a cloud-based IT environment that Oracle deploys, manages, supports and upgrades for the customer and that a customer may access uïŋ―lizing common web browsers via a broad spectrum of devices. 

Oracle Cloud Services are designed to be rapidly deployable to enable customers shorter ïŋ―me to innovaïŋ―on; intuiïŋ―ve for casual and experienced users; easily maintainable to reduce upgrade, integraïŋ―on and tesïŋ―ng work; connectable among differing deployment models to enable interoperability and extensibility to easily move workloads among the Oracle Cloud and other IT and cloud environments; cost-effecïŋ―ve by lowering upfront customer investments and implemenïŋ―ng usage-based resource consumpïŋ―on costs; and highly secure, standards-based and reliable. 

Oracle cloud license and on-premise license deployment offerings include Oracle Applicaïŋ―ons, Oracle Database and Oracle Middleware soïŋ―ware offerings, among others, which customers deploy using IT infrastructure from the Oracle Cloud or their own cloud-based or on-premise IT environments. Substanïŋ―ally all customers opt to purchase license support contracts when they purchase an Oracle license. 

Oracle hardware products include Oracle Engineered Systems, servers, storage and industry-specific products, among others. Customers generally opt to purchase hardware support contracts when they purchase Oracle hardware products. Oracle also offers professional services to assist our customers and partners to maximize the performance of their investments in Oracle products and services. Providing choice and flexibility to Oracle customers as to when and how they deploy Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies is an important element of our corporate strategy. We believe that offering customers broad, comprehensive, flexible and interoperable deployment models for Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies is important to our growth strategy and beïŋ―er addresses customer needs relaïŋ―ve to our compeïŋ―tors, many of whom provide fewer offerings, more restricïŋ―ve deployment models and less flexibility for a customerâs transiïŋ―on to cloud-based IT environments. 

Our investments in, and innovaïŋ―on with respect to, Oracle products and services that we offer through our three businesses (cloud and license, hardware and services businesses, described further below) are another important element of our corporate strategy. In fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, we invested $8.6 billion, $7.2 billion and $6.5 billion, respecïŋ―vely, in research and development to enhance our exisïŋ―ng porïŋ―olio of offerings and to develop new technologies and services. We have a deep understanding as to how applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies interact and funcïŋ―on with one another, including through the use of OCI to power our Oracle Fusion SaaS Applicaïŋ―ons, which we and our customers use to run internal business processes. We focus our development efforts

## **Oracle Applicaïŋ―ons and Infrastructure Technologies** 

Oracleâs comprehensive porïŋ―olio of applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies is designed to address an organizaïŋ―onâs IT environment needs, including business process, infrastructure and applicaïŋ―ons development requirements, among others. Oracle technologies are based upon industry standards and are designed to be enterprise-grade, reliable, scalable and secure. Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies, including database and middleware soïŋ―ware as well as enterprise applicaïŋ―ons, virtualizaïŋ―on, clustering, large-scale systems management and related infrastructure products and services, are the building blocks of Oracle Cloud Services, our partnersâ cloud services and our customersâ cloud IT environments. Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings are marketed and sold through our cloud and license and hardware businesses and are delivered through the Oracle Cloud or through other IT deployment models, including cloud-based, hybrid and on-premise deployments. 

We believe that our Oracle Cloud Services offerings are opportuniïŋ―es for us to conïŋ―nue to expand our cloud and license business. We believe that our customers increasingly recognize the value of access to the latest versions of Oracle cloud-based applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure capabiliïŋ―es via a lower cost, rapidly deployable, flexible and interoperable services model that Oracle provisions, manages, upgrades and maintains on our customersâ behalf. We believe that we can market and sell our Oracle Cloud Services offerings together to help new and exisïŋ―ng customers migrate their extensive installed base of onpremise and cloud-based applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies to the Oracle Cloud and we believe we are in the early stages of what we expect will be a material migraïŋ―on of our exisïŋ―ng Oracle customer base from on-premise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure products and services to the Oracle Cloud. In addiïŋ―on, we also believe we can market our Oracle Cloud Services offerings to a broader ecosystem of small and medium-sized businesses, non-IT lines of business purchasers, developers and partners due to the highly available, intuiïŋ―ve design, ease of access, low touch and low cost characterisïŋ―cs of the Oracle Cloud.

## _**Oracle Cloud Soïŋ―ware-as-a-Service (SaaS)**_ 

Oracleâs broad spectrum of Oracle Cloud SaaS offerings provides customers a choice of soïŋ―ware applicaïŋ―ons that are delivered via a cloud-based IT environment that we deploy, manage, upgrade and support and that customers purchase by entering into a subscripïŋ―on agreement with us for a stated period. Customers access Oracle Cloud SaaS offerings uïŋ―lizing common web browsers via a broad spectrum of devices. Our SaaS offerings are built upon open industry standards such as SQL, Java and HTML5 for easier applicaïŋ―on accessibility, integraïŋ―on and development. Our SaaS offerings represent an industry leading business innovaïŋ―on plaïŋ―orm, leveraging Oracleâs Next-Generaïŋ―on Cloud Infrastructure, and include a broad suite of modular, next-generaïŋ―on cloud soïŋ―ware applicaïŋ―ons spanning all core business funcïŋ―ons, including, among others: 

- Oracle Fusion Cloud Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP), which is designed to be a complete, global and integrated ERP soluïŋ―on to help organizaïŋ―ons improve decision making and workforce producïŋ―vity, and to opïŋ―mize back-office operaïŋ―ons by uïŋ―lizing a single data and security model with a common user interface; 

- Oracle Fusion Cloud Enterprise Performance Management (EPM), which is designed to analyze financial performance, drive accurate and agile financial plans, opïŋ―mize the financial close and consolidaïŋ―on process, streamline account reconciliaïŋ―on and saïŋ―sfy an organizaïŋ―onâs reporïŋ―ng requirements;

## Oracle Autonomous Database 

Oracle Autonomous Database is designed to deliver performance and scale for enterprise database workloads with automated database operaïŋ―ons and policyand machine learning-driven opïŋ―mizaïŋ―on by combining certain Oracle infrastructure technologies, including the Oracle Database, Oracleâs Next-Generaïŋ―on Cloud Infrastructure, Oracle Exadata, and naïŋ―ve machine learning capabiliïŋ―es, among others. Oracle Autonomous Database is engineered to lower labor costs and reduce human error while using machine learning-driven diagnosïŋ―cs for fault predicïŋ―on and error handling and is also engineered to provide automaïŋ―c threat detecïŋ―on and remediaïŋ―on. ## **Compeïŋ―ïŋ―on** 

We face intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on in all aspects of our business. The nature of the IT industry creates a compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve landscape that is constantly evolving as firms emerge, expand or are acquired, as technology evolves and as customer demands and compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve pressures otherwise change.

## **Item 1A. Risk Factors** 

We operate in rapidly changing economic and technological environments that present numerous risks, many of which are driven by factors that we cannot control or predict. The following discussion, as well as our discussion in Item 7 Managementâs Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condiïŋ―on and Results of Operaïŋ―ons, highlights some of these risks. The risks described below are not exhausïŋ―ve and you should carefully consider these risks and uncertainïŋ―es before invesïŋ―ng in our securiïŋ―es. 

## **Business and Operaïŋ―onal Risks** 

_**We may be unsuccessful in developing and selling new products and services, integraïŋ―ng acquired products and services and enhancing our exisïŋ―ng products and services.**_ Rapid technological advances, intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on, changing delivery models and evolving standards in computer hardware and soïŋ―ware development and communicaïŋ―ons infrastructure, changing and increasingly sophisïŋ―cated customer needs and frequent new product introducïŋ―ons and enhancements characterize the industries in which we compete. If we are unable to develop new or sufficiently differenïŋ―ated products and services, enhance and improve our product offerings and support services in a ïŋ―mely manner or posiïŋ―on and price our products and services to meet demand, customers may not purchase or subscribe to our license, hardware or cloud offerings or renew license support, hardware support or cloud subscripïŋ―ons contracts. Renewals of these contracts are important to our future success. In addiïŋ―on, we cannot provide any assurance that the standards on which we choose to develop new products will allow us to compete effecïŋ―vely for business opportuniïŋ―es in emerging areas. 

We have conïŋ―nued to refresh and release new offerings of our cloud products and services. Machine learning and AI are increasingly driving innovaïŋ―ons in technology, but if they fail to operate as anïŋ―cipated or our other products do not perform as promised, our business and reputaïŋ―on may be harmed. In addiïŋ―on, our business may be adversely affected if: 

- we do not conïŋ―nue to develop and release new or enhanced products and services within the anïŋ―cipated ïŋ―me frames; 

- infrastructure costs to deliver new or enhanced products and services take longer or result in greater costs than anïŋ―cipated; 

- we are unable to increase our exisïŋ―ng data center capacity or establish data centers in new geographic locaïŋ―ons in a ïŋ―mely manner to meet current or expected customer demand; 

- we fail to meet our contractual service level commitments; 

- there is a delay in market acceptance of and difficulty in transiïŋ―oning new and exisïŋ―ng customers to new, enhanced or acquired product lines or services; 

- sancïŋ―ons, export controls or other regulatory, legislaïŋ―ve or other barriers prevent us from serving certain customers or restrict our customers from operaïŋ―ng in specific jurisdicïŋ―ons; 

- there are changes in IT trends that we do not adequately anïŋ―cipate or ïŋ―mely address with our product development efforts; 

- we do not opïŋ―mize complementary product lines and services in a ïŋ―mely manner; or

- we fail to adequately integrate, support or enhance acquired product lines or services. 

In addiïŋ―on, our profitability and revenues could be adversely impacted if we lost one or more of our key customers for any reason, including as a result of any of the factors discussed above. Any such loss could also limit or reduce our growth in future periods. 

_**If we do not successfully execute our Oracle Cloud strategy, including our offerings of Oracle Cloud Services, our revenues and profitability may decline.**_ We provide our cloud and other offerings to customers worldwide via a variety of deployment models, including via our cloud-based SaaS and OCI offerings. As these business models conïŋ―nue to evolve, we may not be able to compete effecïŋ―vely, generate significant revenues or maintain the profitability of our cloud offerings. Addiïŋ―onally, the increasing prevalence of cloud and SaaS delivery models offered by us and our compeïŋ―tors may unfavorably impact the pricing of our cloud and license offerings. If we do not successfully execute our cloud compuïŋ―ng strategy or anïŋ―cipate the cloud compuïŋ―ng needs of our customers, our reputaïŋ―on as a cloud services provider could be harmed and our revenues and profitability could decline. 

As customer demand for our cloud offerings increases, we experience volaïŋ―lity in our reported revenues and operaïŋ―ng results due to the differences in ïŋ―ming of revenue recogniïŋ―on between our cloud license and on-premise license, and hardware product arrangements relaïŋ―ve to our cloud offering arrangements. Customers predominantly purchase our cloud offerings on a subscripïŋ―on basis and revenues from these offerings are generally recognized ratably or as services are consumed over the terms of the subscripïŋ―ons. Consequently, any deterioraïŋ―on in sales acïŋ―vity associated with our cloud offerings may not be immediately observable in our consolidated statement of operaïŋ―ons. This is in contrast to revenues associated with our license and hardware product arrangements, which are generally recognized in full at the ïŋ―me of delivery of the related licenses and hardware products. In addiïŋ―on, we may not be able to accurately anïŋ―cipate customer transiïŋ―ons from or be able to sufficiently backfill reduced customer demand for our license, hardware and support offerings relaïŋ―ve to the expected increase in customer adopïŋ―on of and demand for our Oracle Cloud Services, which could adversely affect our revenues and profitability. 

As a part of our Oracle Cloud strategy, we plan our investment levels based on esïŋ―mates of future revenues and future anïŋ―cipated rates of growth. In recent periods, our cloud services and license support expenses have grown to meet current and expected demand for our cloud offerings, including investments to increase our exisïŋ―ng data center capacity and to establish data centers in new geographic locaïŋ―ons. In connecïŋ―on with these investments, we entered, and expect to conïŋ―nue to enter, into long-term operaïŋ―ng lease commitments with third party data center providers that generally require us to pay significant contract terminaïŋ―on fees to early exit such obligaïŋ―ons should our strategies change, which could adversely impact our profitability and cash flows. In addiïŋ―on, we ouïŋ―it these data centers with equipment and improvements that we typically depreciate over their esïŋ―mated useful lives, which could be shortened should our cloud strategies change, which could adversely affect our profitability. 

_**Our products and services may not funcïŋ―on properly if we experience significant coding, manufacturing or configuraïŋ―on errors in our cloud, license and hardware offerings.**_ Despite tesïŋ―ng prior to the release and throughout the lifecycle of a product or service, our cloud, license and hardware offerings someïŋ―mes contain coding, manufacturing or configuraïŋ―on errors that can impact their funcïŋ―on, performance and security, and result in other negaïŋ―ve consequences. The detecïŋ―on and correcïŋ―on of any errors in released cloud, license or hardware offerings can be ïŋ―me consuming and costly. Errors in our cloud, license or hardware offerings could affect their ability to properly funcïŋ―on, integrate or operate with other cloud, license or hardware offerings, could result in service interrupïŋ―ons, delays or outages of our cloud offerings, could create security vulnerabiliïŋ―es in our products or services, could delay the development or release of new products or services or new versions of products or services, and could adversely affect market acceptance of our products or services. This includes third-party soïŋ―ware products or services incorporated into our own. If we experience any of these errors, or if there are delays in releasing our cloud, license or hardware offerings or new versions of these offerings, our sales could be affected and revenues could decline. In addiïŋ―on, we run Oracleâs business operaïŋ―ons as well as cloud and other services that we offer to our customers on our products and networks. Therefore, any flaws could affect our and our customersâ abiliïŋ―es to conduct business operaïŋ―ons and to ensure accuracy in financial processes and reporïŋ―ng, and may result in unanïŋ―cipated costs and interrupïŋ―ons. could expose us to product liability, performance and warranty claims as well as significant harm to our brand and reputaïŋ―on, which could impact our future sales. 

_**If we are unable to compete effecïŋ―vely, the results of operaïŋ―ons and prospects for our business could be harmed.**_ We face intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on in all aspects of our business. The nature of the IT industry creates a compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve landscape that is constantly evolving as firms emerge, expand or are acquired, as technology evolves and as delivery models change. Our enterprise cloud, license and hardware offerings compete directly with certain offerings from some of the largest and most compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve companies in the world. In addiïŋ―on, due to the low barriers to entry in many of our market segments, new technologies and new and growing compeïŋ―tors frequently emerge to challenge our offerings. We believe many vendors spend amounts in excess of what Oracle spends to develop and market applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies including databases, middleware products, applicaïŋ―on development tools, business applicaïŋ―ons, collaboraïŋ―on products and business intelligence, compute, storage and networking products, among others, which compete with Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings. 

In addiïŋ―on, use of our compeïŋ―torsâ technologies can influence a customerâs purchasing decision or create an environment that makes it less efficient to uïŋ―lize or migrate to Oracle products and services. For example, we offer our customers mulïŋ―cloud services whereby our customers can combine cloud services from mulïŋ―ple clouds with the goal of opïŋ―mizing cost, funcïŋ―onality and performance. OCIâs mulïŋ―cloud services work with a number of our compeïŋ―torsâ products, including Microsoïŋ― Azure, Amazon Web Services and Google Cloud Plaïŋ―orm. This mulïŋ―cloud strategy could lead our customers to migrate away from our cloud offerings to our compeïŋ―torsâ products, which could adversely affect our revenues and profitability. 

Our compeïŋ―tors may also adopt business pracïŋ―ces that provide customers access to compeïŋ―ng products and services on terms that we may not generally find acceptable, which may convince customers to purchase compeïŋ―tor products and services. We could lose customers if our compeïŋ―tors introduce new compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve products, add new funcïŋ―onality, acquire compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve products, reduce prices, beïŋ―er execute on their sales and markeïŋ―ng strategies, offer more flexible business pracïŋ―ces, provide debt or equity financing to customers or form strategic alliances with other companies. Mergers, consolidaïŋ―ons or alliances among our compeïŋ―tors, or acquisiïŋ―ons of our compeïŋ―tors by large companies may result in increased compeïŋ―ïŋ―on. 

If our compeïŋ―tors offer deep discounts on certain products or services or develop products that the marketplace considers more valuable, we may need to lower prices, introduce pricing models and offerings or offer other terms that are less favorable to us, in order to compete successfully. Any such changes may reduce revenues and margins and could adversely affect operaïŋ―ng results. Addiïŋ―onally, the increasing prevalence of cloud delivery models offered by us and our compeïŋ―tors may unfavorably impact the pricing of our other cloud and license, hardware and services offerings, and we may also incur increased cloud delivery expenses as we expand our cloud operaïŋ―ons and update our infrastructure, all of which could reduce our revenues and profitability. Our license support fees and hardware support fees are generally priced as a percentage of our net license fees and net new hardware products fees, respecïŋ―vely. Our compeïŋ―tors may offer lower pricing on their support offerings, which could put pressure on us to further discount our offerings. 

Changes to our prices and pricing policies could cause our revenues to decline or be delayed as our sales force implements and our customers adjust to the new pricing policies. Some of our compeïŋ―tors may bundle products for promoïŋ―onal purposes or as a long-term pricing strategy, commit to large customer deployments at prices that are unprofitable, or provide guarantees of prices and product implementaïŋ―ons. These pracïŋ―ces could, over ïŋ―me, significantly constrain the prices that we can charge for certain of our products. If we do not adapt our pricing models to reflect changes in customer use of our products or changes in customer demand, our revenues could decrease. The increase in open source soïŋ―ware distribuïŋ―on may also cause us to change our pricing models. 

_**Any failure to offer high-quality technical support services may adversely affect our relaïŋ―onships with our customers and our financial results**_ . ## **Legal and Regulatory Risks** 

_**Adverse liïŋ―gaïŋ―on results could affect our business.**_ We are subject to various legal proceedings. Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on can be lengthy, expensive and disrupïŋ―ve to our operaïŋ―ons, and can divert our managementâs aïŋ―enïŋ―on away from running our core business. ## **Financial Risks** 

_**Our operaïŋ―ons can be difficult for us to predict because our quarterly results of operaïŋ―ons may fluctuate significantly based on a number of factors.**_ Our revenues, parïŋ―cularly certain of our cloud license and on-premise license revenues and hardware revenues, can be difficult to forecast. In addiïŋ―on, sudden shiïŋ―s in regional or global economic or poliïŋ―cal acïŋ―vity may cause our sales forecasts to be inaccurate. 

In addiïŋ―on, we hold a porïŋ―olio of publicly traded and privately held equity investments. Changes in the fair values of these investments are recorded as unrealized gains or losses as a component of consolidated net income in each period. The ïŋ―ming and amount of changes in fair value, if any, of these investments depends on factors beyond our control, including the perceived and actual performance of the companies or funds in which we invest. Changes in the fair values of these investments are also subject to the general condiïŋ―ons of public and private equity markets, which are uncertain and have in the past varied, and may in the future vary, materially by period. Changes in the fair values of these investments have contributed, and may in the future contribute, to volaïŋ―lity in our net income that is not reflecïŋ―ve of our core businesses. 

_**Changes in currency exchange rates can adversely affect customer demand and our revenue and profitability.**_ We conduct a significant number of transacïŋ―ons and hold cash in currencies other than the U.S. Dollar. In addiïŋ―on, our reported assets generally are adversely affected when the dollar strengthens relaïŋ―ve to other currencies as a porïŋ―on of our consolidated cash and bank deposits, among other assets, are held in foreign currencies and reported in U.S. Dollars. 

In addiïŋ―on, we incur foreign currency transacïŋ―on gains and losses, primarily related to sublicense fees and other intercompany agreements among us and our subsidiaries that we expect to cash seïŋ―le in the near term, which are charged to earnings in the period incurred. As part of this program, we enter into foreign currency forward contracts so that increases or decreases in our foreign currency exposures are offset at least in part by gains or losses on the foreign currency forward contracts in an effort to miïŋ―gate the risks and volaïŋ―lity associated with our foreign currency transacïŋ―on gains or losses. ## **General Risks** 

_**Economic, poliïŋ―cal and market condiïŋ―ons can adversely affect our business, results of operaïŋ―ons and financial condiïŋ―on, including our revenue growth and profitability, which in turn could adversely affect our stock price.**_ Our business is influenced by a range of factors that are beyond our control and that we have no comparaïŋ―ve advantage in forecasïŋ―ng. - general economic and business condiïŋ―ons; 

- overall demand for enterprise cloud, license and hardware products and services; 

- governmental budgetary constraints or shiïŋ―s in government spending prioriïŋ―es; and 

- general legal, regulatory and poliïŋ―cal developments. 

Macroeconomic developments such as the global or regional economic effects resulïŋ―ng from increasing inflaïŋ―on rates, limited liquidity, adverse developments affecïŋ―ng financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons, the current Russia-Ukraine war and related economic curtailment iniïŋ―aïŋ―ves, evolving trade policies between the U.S. and internaïŋ―onal trade partners, or the occurrence of similar events in other countries that lead to uncertainty or instability in economic, poliïŋ―cal or market condiïŋ―ons could negaïŋ―vely affect our business, operaïŋ―ng results, financial condiïŋ―on and outlook, which, in turn, could adversely affect our stock price. Any general weakening of, and related declining corporate confidence in, the global economy or the curtailment of government or corporate spending could cause current or potenïŋ―al customers to reduce or eliminate their IT budgets and spending, which could cause customers to delay, decrease or cancel purchases of our products and services or cause customers not to pay us or to delay paying us for previously purchased products and services. If any parïŋ―es with whom we conduct business or invest our cash or cash equivalents are unable to meet their obligaïŋ―ons to us, our business could be adversely affected. Bank failures or issues in the broader U.S. or global financial systems may have an impact on the broader capital markets and, in turn, our ability to access those markets. 

In addiïŋ―on, internaïŋ―onal, regional or domesïŋ―c poliïŋ―cal unrest and the related potenïŋ―al impact on global stability, terrorist aïŋ―acks and the potenïŋ―al for other hosïŋ―liïŋ―es in various parts of the world, public health crises and natural disasters conïŋ―nue to contribute to a climate of economic and poliïŋ―cal uncertainty that could adversely affect our results of operaïŋ―ons and financial condiïŋ―on, including our revenue growth and profitability. These factors generally have the strongest effect on our sales of cloud license and on-premise license, hardware and related services and, to a lesser extent, also may affect our renewal rates for license support and our subscripïŋ―on-based cloud offerings. 

_**Business disrupïŋ―ons could adversely affect our operaïŋ―ng results.**_ A significant porïŋ―on of our criïŋ―cal business operaïŋ―ons are concentrated in a few geographic areas, some of which include emerging market internaïŋ―onal locaïŋ―ons that may be less stable relaïŋ―ve to running such business operaïŋ―ons solely within the U.S. We are a highly automated business and a disrupïŋ―on or failure of our systems, supply chains and processes could cause delays in compleïŋ―ng sales, providing services, including some of our cloud offerings, and enabling a seamless customer experience with respect to our customer facing back-office processes. A major natural disaster, poliïŋ―cal, social or other disrupïŋ―on to infrastructure that supports our operaïŋ―ons or other catastrophic event or the effects of climate change (such as increased storm severity, drought and pandemics) that results in the destrucïŋ―on or disrupïŋ―on of any of our criïŋ―cal business operaïŋ―ons, supply chains or IT systems could severely affect our ability to conduct normal business operaïŋ―ons and, as a result, our future operaïŋ―ng results could be materially and adversely affected.

## **Item 7. Managementâs Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condiïŋ―on and Results of Operaïŋ―ons**

## **Business Overview** 

Oracle provides products and services that address enterprise informaïŋ―on technology (IT) environments. Our products and services include enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure offerings that are delivered worldwide through a variety of flexible and interoperable IT deployment models. These models include on-premise, cloud-based and hybrid deployments (an approach that combines both on-premise and cloud-based deployments). Accordingly, we offer choice and flexibility to our customers and facilitate the product, service and deployment combinaïŋ―ons that best suit our customersâ needs. Through our worldwide sales force and Oracle Partner Network, we sell to customers all over the world including businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and resellers. 

We have three businesses: cloud and license; hardware; and services; each of which comprises a single operaïŋ―ng segment. The descripïŋ―ons set forth below as a part of this Item 7 Managementâs Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condiïŋ―on and Results of Operaïŋ―ons and the informaïŋ―on contained within Item 1 Business and Note 14 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements included elsewhere in this Annual Report provide addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on related to our businesses and operaïŋ―ng segments and align to how our chief operaïŋ―ng decision makers (CODMs), which include our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer and Chief Technology Officer, view our operaïŋ―ng results and allocate resources. 

## **Cloud and License Business** 

Our cloud and license business, which represented 83% and 85% of our total revenues in fiscal 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely, markets, sells and delivers a broad spectrum of enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies through our cloud and license offerings. Revenue streams included in our cloud and license business are: 

- Cloud services and license support revenues, which include: 

   - license support revenues, which are earned by providing Oracle license support services to customers that have elected to purchase support services in connecïŋ―on with the purchase of Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure licenses for use in cloud, on-premise and other IT environments. Substanïŋ―ally all license support customers renew their support contracts with us upon expiraïŋ―on in order to conïŋ―nue to benefit from technical support services and the periodic issuance of unspecified updates and enhancements, which current license support customers are enïŋ―tled to receive. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net fees paid by the customer to purchase a cloud license and/or on-premise license; are generally billed in advance of the support services being performed; are generally renewed at the customerâs opïŋ―on; and are generally recognized as revenues ratably over the contractual period that the support services are provided, which is generally one year; and 

   - cloud services revenues, which are earned by providing customers access to Oracle Cloud applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies via cloud-based deployment models that Oracle develops, provides unspecified updates and enhancements for, deploys, hosts, manages and supports and that customers access by entering into a subscripïŋ―on agreement with us for a stated period. Oracle Cloud Services arrangements are generally billed in advance of the cloud services being performed; generally have duraïŋ―ons of one to three years; are generally renewed at the customerâs opïŋ―on; and are generally

   - recognized as revenues ratably over the contractual period of the cloud contract or, in the case of usage model contracts, as the cloud services are consumed over ïŋ―me. 

- Cloud license and on-premise license revenues, which include revenues from the licensing of our soïŋ―ware products including Oracle Applicaïŋ―ons, Oracle Database, Oracle Middleware and Java, among others, which our customers deploy within cloud-based, on-premise or other IT environments. Our cloud license and on-premise license transacïŋ―ons are generally perpetual in nature and are generally recognized as revenues up front at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the customer to download and use. Revenues from usage-based royalty arrangements for disïŋ―nct cloud licenses and on-premise licenses are recognized at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware end user usage occurs. The ïŋ―ming of a few large license transacïŋ―ons can substanïŋ―ally affect our quarterly license revenues due to the point-in-ïŋ―me nature of revenue recogniïŋ―on for license transacïŋ―ons, which is different than the typical revenue recogniïŋ―on païŋ―ern for our cloud services and license support revenues in which revenues are generally recognized ratably over the contractual terms. Cloud license and on-premise license customers have the opïŋ―on to purchase and renew license support contracts, as further described above. 

Providing choice and flexibility to our customers as to when and how they deploy Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies are important elements of our corporate strategy. In recent periods, customer demand for our applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies delivered through our Oracle Cloud Services has increased. The proporïŋ―on of our cloud services revenues relaïŋ―ve to our total revenues has increased and we expect this trend to conïŋ―nue. Cloud services revenues represented 32%, 25% and 22% of our total revenues during fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely. 

Our cloud and license businessâ revenue growth is affected by many factors, including the strength of general economic and business condiïŋ―ons; governmental budgetary constraints; the strategy for and compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve posiïŋ―on of our offerings; customer saïŋ―sfacïŋ―on with our offerings; the conïŋ―nued renewal of our cloud services and license support customer contracts by the customer contract base; substanïŋ―ally all customers conïŋ―nuing to purchase license support contracts in connecïŋ―on with their license purchases; the pricing of license support contracts sold in connecïŋ―on with the sales of licenses; the pricing, amounts and volumes of licenses and cloud services sold; our ability to manage Oracle Cloud capacity requirements to meet exisïŋ―ng and prospecïŋ―ve customer demand; and foreign currency rate fluctuaïŋ―ons. 

On a constant currency basis, we expect that our total cloud and license revenues generally will conïŋ―nue to increase due to:

## **Hardware Business** 

Our hardware business, which represented 6% and 7% of our total revenues in fiscal 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely, provides a broad selecïŋ―on of enterprise hardware products and hardware-related soïŋ―ware products including Oracle Engineered Systems, servers, storage, industry-specific hardware offerings, operaïŋ―ng systems, virtualizaïŋ―on, management and other hardware-related soïŋ―ware, and related hardware support. ## **Criïŋ―cal Accounïŋ―ng Policies and Esïŋ―mates** 

Our consolidated financial statements are prepared in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles (GAAP) as set forth in the Financial Accounïŋ―ng Standards Boardâs Accounïŋ―ng Standards Codificaïŋ―on (ASC), and we consider various staff accounïŋ―ng bulleïŋ―ns and other applicable guidance issued by the SEC. GAAP, as set forth within the ASC, requires us to make certain esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons. We believe that the esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons upon which we rely are reasonable based upon informaïŋ―on available to us at the ïŋ―me that these esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons are made. These esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons can affect the reported amounts of assets and liabiliïŋ―es as of the date of the financial statements as well as the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the periods presented. To the extent that there are differences between these esïŋ―mates, judgments or assumpïŋ―ons and actual results, our financial statements will be affected. The accounïŋ―ng policies that reflect our more significant esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons and which we believe are the most criïŋ―cal to aid in fully understanding and evaluaïŋ―ng our reported financial results include: 

- Revenue Recogniïŋ―on; 

- Business Combinaïŋ―ons; 

- Goodwill and Intangible AssetsâImpairment Assessments; 

- Accounïŋ―ng for Income Taxes; and 

- Legal and Other Conïŋ―ngencies. 

Our senior management has reviewed our criïŋ―cal accounïŋ―ng policies and related disclosures with the Finance and Audit Commiïŋ―ee of the Board of Directors. Refer to Note 1 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements included elsewhere in this Annual Report for more discussion of our criïŋ―cal and other accounïŋ―ng policies. There were no significant changes to our criïŋ―cal accounïŋ―ng policies and esïŋ―mates from the prior year. 

## _**Revenue Recogniïŋ―on**_ 

The most criïŋ―cal judgments required in applying ASC 606, _Revenue Recogniïŋ―on from Customers_ , and our revenue recogniïŋ―on policy relate to the determinaïŋ―on of disïŋ―nct performance obligaïŋ―ons and the evaluaïŋ―on of the standalone selling price (SSP) for each performance obligaïŋ―on. 

Many of our customer contracts include mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons. Judgment is required in determining whether each performance obligaïŋ―on within a customer contract is disïŋ―nct. Oracle products and services generally funcïŋ―on on a standalone basis and do not require a significant amount of integraïŋ―on or interdependency. Therefore, mulïŋ―ple products and services contained within a customer contract are generally considered to be disïŋ―nct and are not combined for revenue recogniïŋ―on purposes. We allocate the transacïŋ―on price for each customer contract to each performance obligaïŋ―on based on the relaïŋ―ve SSP (the determinaïŋ―on of SSP is discussed below) for each 

38 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

performance obligaïŋ―on within each contract. We recognize the amount of transacïŋ―on price allocated to each performance obligaïŋ―on within a customer contract as revenue as each performance obligaïŋ―on is saïŋ―sfied. 

We use historical sales transacïŋ―on data and judgment, among other factors, in determining the SSP for products and services. For substanïŋ―ally all performance obligaïŋ―ons except cloud licenses and on-premise licenses, we are able to establish the SSP based on the observable prices of products or services sold separately in comparable circumstances to similar customers. We typically establish an SSP range for our products and services, which is reassessed on a periodic basis or when facts and circumstances change. SSP for our products and services can evolve over ïŋ―me due to changes in our pricing pracïŋ―ces that are influenced by intense compeïŋ―ïŋ―on, changes in demand for our products and services, and economic factors, among others. Our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses have not historically been sold on a standalone basis, as substanïŋ―ally all customers elect to purchase license support contracts at the ïŋ―me of a license purchase. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net fees paid by the customer to purchase the license. We are unable to establish the SSP for our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses based on observable prices given the same products are sold for a broad range of amounts (that is, the selling price is highly variable) and a representaïŋ―ve SSP is not discernible from past transacïŋ―ons or other observable evidence. As a result, the SSP for a cloud license and an on-premise license included in a contract with mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons is generally determined by applying a residual approach whereby all other performance obligaïŋ―ons within a contract are first allocated a porïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price based upon their respecïŋ―ve SSPs, with any residual amount of transacïŋ―on price allocated to cloud license and on-premise license revenues. 

## _**Business Combinaïŋ―ons**_ 

We apply the provisions of ASC 805, _Business Combinaïŋ―ons_ (ASC 805), in accounïŋ―ng for our acquisiïŋ―ons. ASC 805 requires that we evaluate whether a transacïŋ―on pertains to an acquisiïŋ―on of assets, or to an acquisiïŋ―on of a business. A business is defined as an integrated set of assets and acïŋ―viïŋ―es that is capable of being conducted and managed for the purpose of providing a return to investors. Asset acquisiïŋ―ons are accounted for by allocaïŋ―ng the cost of the acquisiïŋ―on to the individual assets and liabiliïŋ―es assumed on a relaïŋ―ve fair value basis; whereas the acquisiïŋ―on of a business requires us to recognize separately from goodwill the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values. Goodwill as of the acquisiïŋ―on date is measured as the excess of consideraïŋ―on transferred over the net of the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values of the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed. While we use our best esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons to accurately value assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the acquisiïŋ―on date as well as any conïŋ―ngent consideraïŋ―on, where applicable, our esïŋ―mates are inherently uncertain and subject to refinement. As a result, during the measurement period, which may be up to one year from the business acquisiïŋ―on date, we record adjustments to the assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed with the corresponding offset to goodwill. Upon the conclusion of a business acquisiïŋ―onâs measurement period or final determinaïŋ―on of the values of assets acquired or liabiliïŋ―es assumed, whichever comes first, any subsequent adjustments are recorded to our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. 

Accounïŋ―ng for business combinaïŋ―ons requires our management to make significant esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons, especially at the acquisiïŋ―on date, including our esïŋ―mates for intangible assets, pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngencies and any conïŋ―ngent consideraïŋ―on, where applicable. Although we believe that the assumpïŋ―ons and esïŋ―mates we have made in the past have been reasonable and appropriate, they are based in part on historical experience and informaïŋ―on obtained from the management of the acquired companies and are inherently uncertain. Unanïŋ―cipated events and circumstances may occur that may affect the accuracy or validity of such assumpïŋ―ons, esïŋ―mates or actual results. 

For a given business acquisiïŋ―on, we may idenïŋ―fy certain pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngencies as of the acquisiïŋ―on date and may extend our review and evaluaïŋ―on of these pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngencies throughout the measurement period in order to obtain sufficient informaïŋ―on to assess whether we include these conïŋ―ngencies as a part of the fair value esïŋ―mates of assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed and, if so, to determine their esïŋ―mated amounts. 

If we cannot reasonably determine the fair value of a non-income tax related pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngency by the end of the measurement period, which is generally the case given the nature of such maïŋ―ers, we will recognize an asset or a liability for such pre-acquisiïŋ―on conïŋ―ngency if: (1) it is probable that an asset existed or a liability had been incurred at the acquisiïŋ―on date and (2) the amount of the asset or liability can be reasonably esïŋ―mated. Subsequent

In addiïŋ―on, uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons and tax related valuaïŋ―on allowances assumed in a business combinaïŋ―on are iniïŋ―ally esïŋ―mated as of the acquisiïŋ―on date. ## _**Goodwill and Intangible AssetsâImpairment Assessments**_ 

We review goodwill for impairment annually and whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate its carrying value may not be recoverable. We make certain judgments and assumpïŋ―ons to determine our reporïŋ―ng units and in allocaïŋ―ng shared assets and liabiliïŋ―es to determine the carrying values for each of our reporïŋ―ng units. 

Judgment in the assessment of qualitaïŋ―ve factors of impairment include cost factors; financial performance; legal, regulatory, contractual, poliïŋ―cal, business, and other factors; enïŋ―ty specific factors; industry and market consideraïŋ―ons, macroeconomic condiïŋ―ons, and other relevant events and factors affecïŋ―ng the reporïŋ―ng unit. To the extent we determine that it is more likely than not that the fair value of the reporïŋ―ng unit is less than its carrying value, a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve test is then performed. 

Performing a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve goodwill impairment test includes the determinaïŋ―on of the fair value of a reporïŋ―ng unit and involves significant esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons. These esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons include, among others, revenue growth rates and operaïŋ―ng margins used to calculate projected future cash flows, risk-adjusted discount rates, future economic and market condiïŋ―ons, and the determinaïŋ―on of appropriate market comparables. 

We make judgments about the recoverability of purchased finite lived intangible assets whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that impairment may exist. In such situaïŋ―ons, we are required to evaluate whether the net book values of our finite lived intangible assets are recoverable. We determine whether finite lived intangible assets are recoverable based upon the forecasted future cash flows that are expected to be generated by the lowest level associated asset grouping. Assumpïŋ―ons and esïŋ―mates about future values and remaining useful lives of our intangible assets are complex and subjecïŋ―ve and include, among others, forecasted undiscounted cash flows to be generated by certain asset groupings. These assumpïŋ―ons and esïŋ―mates can be affected by a variety of factors, including external factors such as industry and economic trends and internal factors such as changes in our business strategy and our internal forecasts. 

## _**Accounïŋ―ng for Income Taxes**_ 

Judgment is required in determining our worldwide income tax provision. In the ordinary course of a global business, there are many transacïŋ―ons and calculaïŋ―ons where the ulïŋ―mate tax outcome is uncertain. Some of these uncertainïŋ―es arise as a consequence of revenue sharing and cost reimbursement arrangements among related enïŋ―ïŋ―es, the process of idenïŋ―fying items of revenues and expenses that qualify for preferenïŋ―al tax treatment, and the segregaïŋ―on of foreign and domesïŋ―c earnings and expenses to avoid double taxaïŋ―on. Although we believe that our esïŋ―mates are reasonable, the final tax outcome of these maïŋ―ers could be different from that which is reflected in our historical income tax provisions and accruals. Such differences could have a material effect on our income tax provision and net income in the period in which such determinaïŋ―on is made. 

We record a valuaïŋ―on allowance to reduce our deferred tax assets to the amount that is more likely than not to be realized. In order for us to realize our deferred tax assets, we must be able to generate sufficient taxable income in those jurisdicïŋ―ons where the deferred tax assets are located. We consider future growth, forecasted earnings, future taxable income, the mix of earnings in the jurisdicïŋ―ons in which we operate, historical earnings, taxable income in prior years, if carryback is permiïŋ―ed under the law, and prudent and feasible tax planning strategies in determining 

40 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

the need for a valuaïŋ―on allowance. In the event we were to determine that we would not be able to realize all or part of our net deferred tax assets in the future, an adjustment to the deferred tax assets valuaïŋ―on allowance would be charged to earnings in the period in which we make such a determinaïŋ―on, or goodwill would be adjusted at our final determinaïŋ―on of the valuaïŋ―on allowance related to an acquisiïŋ―on within the measurement period. If we later determine that it is more likely than not that the net deferred tax assets would be realized, we would reverse the applicable porïŋ―on of the previously provided valuaïŋ―on allowance as an adjustment to our provision for income taxes at such ïŋ―me. 

We calculate our current and deferred tax provision based on esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons that could differ from the actual results reflected in income tax returns filed during the subsequent year. Adjustments based on filed returns are generally recorded in the period when the tax returns are filed and the global tax implicaïŋ―ons are known, which can materially impact our effecïŋ―ve tax rate. 

The amount of income tax we pay is subject to ongoing audits by federal, state and foreign tax authoriïŋ―es, which oïŋ―en result in proposed assessments. Our esïŋ―mate of the potenïŋ―al outcome for any uncertain tax issue may require certain judgments. A descripïŋ―on of our accounïŋ―ng policies associated with tax related conïŋ―ngencies assumed as a part of a business combinaïŋ―on is provided under âBusiness Combinaïŋ―onsâ above. 

For those tax related conïŋ―ngencies that are not a part of a business combinaïŋ―on, we account for these uncertain tax issues pursuant to ASC 740, _Income Taxes_ , which contains a two-step approach to recognizing and measuring uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. The first step is to determine if the weight of available evidence indicates that it is more likely than not that the tax posiïŋ―on will be sustained in an audit, including resoluïŋ―on of any related appeals or liïŋ―gaïŋ―on processes. The second step is to measure the tax benefit as the largest amount that is more than 50% likely to be realized upon ulïŋ―mate seïŋ―lement. Although we believe that we have adequately reserved for our uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons, no assurance can be given with respect to the final outcome of these maïŋ―ers. We adjust reserves for our uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons due to changing facts and circumstances, such as the closing of a tax audit, judicial rulings, and refinement of esïŋ―mates or realizaïŋ―on of earnings or deducïŋ―ons that differ from our esïŋ―mates. To the extent that the final outcome of these maïŋ―ers is different than the amounts recorded, such differences generally will impact our provision for income taxes in the period in which such a determinaïŋ―on is made. Our provisions for income taxes include the impact of reserve provisions and changes to reserves that are considered appropriate and also include the related interest and penalïŋ―es. 

## _**Legal and Other Conïŋ―ngencies**_ 

We are currently involved in various claims and legal proceedings. Quarterly, we review the status of each significant maïŋ―er and assess our potenïŋ―al financial exposure. A descripïŋ―on of our accounïŋ―ng policies associated with conïŋ―ngencies assumed as a part of a business combinaïŋ―on is provided under âBusiness Combinaïŋ―onsâ above. For legal and other conïŋ―ngencies that are not a part of a business combinaïŋ―on, we accrue a liability for an esïŋ―mated loss if the potenïŋ―al loss from any claim or legal proceeding is considered probable, and the amount can be reasonably esïŋ―mated. Significant judgment is required in both the determinaïŋ―on of probability and the determinaïŋ―on as to whether the amount of an exposure is reasonably esïŋ―mable. Because of uncertainïŋ―es related to these maïŋ―ers, accruals are based only on the best informaïŋ―on available at the ïŋ―me the accruals are made. As addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on becomes available, we reassess the potenïŋ―al liability related to our pending claims and liïŋ―gaïŋ―on and may revise our esïŋ―mates. Such revisions in the esïŋ―mates of the potenïŋ―al liabiliïŋ―es could have a material impact on our results of operaïŋ―ons and financial posiïŋ―on.

## **Constant Currency Presentaïŋ―on**

To present this informaïŋ―on, current and comparaïŋ―ve prior period results for enïŋ―ïŋ―es reporïŋ―ng in currencies other than U.S. Dollars are converted into U.S. Dollars at constant exchange rates (i.e., the rates in effect on May 31, 2022, which was the last day of our prior fiscal year) rather than the actual exchange rates in effect during the respecïŋ―ve periods. For example, if an enïŋ―ty reporïŋ―ng in Euros had revenues of 1.0 million Euros from products sold on May 31, 2023 and 2022, our financial statements would reflect reported revenues of $1.08 million in fiscal 2023 (using 1.08 as the month-end average exchange rate for the period) and $1.07 million in fiscal 2022 (using 1.07 as the month-end average exchange rate for the period).

## **Cloud and License Business** 

Our cloud and license business engages in the sale and markeïŋ―ng of our applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies that are delivered through various deployment models and include: Oracle license support offerings; Oracle Cloud Services offerings; and Oracle cloud license and on-premise license offerings. License support revenues are typically generated through the sale of applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure license support contracts related to cloud licenses and onpremise licenses; are purchased by our customers at their opïŋ―on; and are generally recognized as revenues ratably over the contractual term, which is generally one year. Our cloud services deliver applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies on a subscripïŋ―on basis via cloud-based deployment models that we develop, provide unspecified updates and enhancements for, deploy, host, manage and support. Revenues for our cloud services are generally recognized over the contractual term, which is generally one to three years, or in the case of usage model contracts, as the cloud services are consumed. Cloud license and onpremise license revenues represent fees earned from granïŋ―ng customers licenses, generally on a perpetual basis, to use our database and middleware and our applicaïŋ―ons soïŋ―ware products within cloud and on-premise IT environments and are generally recognized up front at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the customer to download and use. We conïŋ―nue to place significant emphasis, both domesïŋ―cally and internaïŋ―onally, on direct sales through our own sales force. We also conïŋ―nue to market certain of our offerings through indirect channels. Costs associated with our cloud and license business are included in cloud services and license support expenses, and sales and markeïŋ―ng expenses. These costs are largely personnel and infrastructure related including the cost of providing our cloud services and license support offerings, salaries and commissions earned by our sales force for the sale of our cloud and license offerings, and markeïŋ―ng program costs.

## **Hardware Business** 

Our hardware businessâ revenues are generated from the sales of our Oracle Engineered Systems, server, storage, and industry-specific hardware offerings. The hardware product and related soïŋ―ware, such as an operaïŋ―ng system or firmware, are highly interdependent and interrelated and are accounted for as a combined performance obligaïŋ―on. The revenues for this combined performance obligaïŋ―on are generally recognized at the point in ïŋ―me that the hardware product is delivered to the customer and ownership is transferred to the customer. Our hardware business also earns revenues from the sale of hardware support contracts purchased by our customers at their opïŋ―on and that are generally recognized as revenues ratably as the hardware support services are delivered over the contractual term, which is generally one year. The majority of our hardware products are sold through indirect channels such as independent distributors and value-added resellers and we also market and sell our hardware products through our direct sales force. Operaïŋ―ng expenses associated with our hardware business include the cost of hardware products, which consists of expenses for materials and labor used to produce these products by our internal manufacturing operaïŋ―ons or by third-party manufacturers, warranty and related expenses and the impact of periodic changes in inventory valuaïŋ―on, including the impact of inventory determined to be excess and obsolete; the cost of materials used to repair customer products with eligible support contracts; the cost of labor and infrastructure to provide support services; and sales and markeïŋ―ng expenses, which are largely personnel related and include variable compensaïŋ―on earned by our sales force for the sales of our hardware offerings.

## **Stock-Based Awards** 

Our stock-based compensaïŋ―on program is a key component of the compensaïŋ―on package we provide to aïŋ―ract and retain certain of our talented employees and align their interests with the interests of exisïŋ―ng stockholders. 

We recognize that stock-based awards dilute exisïŋ―ng stockholders and have sought to control the number of stock-based awards granted while providing compeïŋ―ïŋ―ve compensaïŋ―on packages. Consistent with these dual goals, our cumulaïŋ―ve potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on since June 1, 2020 has been an annualized rate of 1.8% per year. The potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on percentage is calculated as the average annualized new stock-based awards granted and assumed, net of stock-based awards forfeited by employees leaving the company, divided by the weighted-average outstanding shares during the calculaïŋ―on period. This maximum potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on will only result if all stock-based awards vest and, if applicable, are exercised. Of the outstanding stock opïŋ―ons at May 31, 2023, which generally have a ten-year exercise period, all have exercise prices lower than the market price of our common stock on such date. In recent years, our stock repurchase program has more than offset the diluïŋ―ve effect of our stock-based compensaïŋ―on program. However, we may modify the levels of our stock repurchases in the future depending on a number of factors, including the amount of cash we have available for acquisiïŋ―ons, to pay dividends, to repay or repurchase indebtedness or for other purposes. As of May 31, 2023, the maximum potenïŋ―al diluïŋ―on from all outstanding stock-based awards, regardless of when granted and regardless of whether vested or unvested, was 8.0%. 

During fiscal 2023, the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board of Directors reviewed and approved the annual organizaïŋ―on-wide stock-based award grants to selected employees; all stock-based award grants to senior officers; and any individual grant of restricted stock units of 62,500 or greater. Each member of a separate execuïŋ―ve officer commiïŋ―ee, referred to as the Plan Commiïŋ―ee, was allocated a fiscal 2023 equity budget that could be used throughout the fiscal year to grant equity within his or her organizaïŋ―on, subject to certain limitaïŋ―ons established by the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee.

## **Item 7A. Quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve and Qualitaïŋ―ve Disclosures About Market Risk** 

## **Equity Price Risk** 

## **Marketable and Non-Marketable Equity Investments** 

Our marketable and non-marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments totaled $972 million and $1.1 billion as of May 31, 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely. Our marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments in publicly traded companies are recorded at fair value, which is subject to market price volaïŋ―lity. Our non-marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments in private companies not accounted for under the equity method are adjusted to fair value for observable transacïŋ―ons for idenïŋ―cal or similar investments of the same issuer or for impairment. Our non-marketable equity securiïŋ―es investments accounted for under the equity method, primarily in a related party enïŋ―ty, generally do not fluctuate based on market price changes. However, these equity method investments could be impaired if the carrying value exceeds the fair value and is not expected to recover. The ïŋ―ming and amounts of changes in fair value of our marketable and nonmarketable equity investments depends on factors beyond our control, including the perceived and actual performance of the companies in which we invest. Our non-marketable converïŋ―ble debt investments would be subject to equity price risk in the future when the converïŋ―ble opïŋ―on is exercised. For addiïŋ―onal disclosure regarding the impact to our quarterly results of operaïŋ―ons from investment volaïŋ―lity, please refer to Item 1A Risk Factors included elsewhere in this Annual Report. 

## **Currency Risk** 

## **Foreign Currency Translaïŋ―on Risk** 

As described under âConstant Currency Presentaïŋ―onâ above, our internaïŋ―onal operaïŋ―ons have provided and are expected to conïŋ―nue to provide a significant porïŋ―on of our consolidated revenues and expenses that we report in U.S. Dollars. As a result, our consolidated revenues and expenses are affected and will conïŋ―nue to be affected by changes in the U.S. Dollar against major foreign currencies. Fluctuaïŋ―ons in foreign currencies impact the amount of total assets, liabiliïŋ―es, earnings and cash flows that we report for our foreign subsidiaries upon the translaïŋ―on of these amounts into U.S. Dollars for, and as of the end of, each reporïŋ―ng period. In parïŋ―cular, the strengthening of the U.S. Dollar generally will reduce the reported amount of our foreign-denominated cash, cash equivalents, trade receivables, total revenues and total expenses that we translate into U.S. Dollars and report in our consolidated financial statements for, and as of the end of, each reporïŋ―ng period. 

## **Foreign Currency Transacïŋ―on Risk** 

We transact business in various foreign currencies. Our foreign currency exposures primarily arise from various intercompany transacïŋ―ons. Our principal currency exposures include the Australian Dollar, Brazilian Real, Euro, Japanese Yen and Saudi Riyal. We have established a program that primarily uïŋ―lizes foreign currency forward contracts to offset the risks that arise from the aforemenïŋ―oned transacïŋ―ons. Under this program, our strategy is to enter into foreign currency forward contracts for major currencies in which we have an exposure so that increases or decreases in our foreign currency exposures are offset by gains or losses on the foreign currency forward contracts which miïŋ―gate the risks and volaïŋ―lity associated with our foreign currency transacïŋ―ons. We may suspend this program from ïŋ―me to ïŋ―me. Our foreign currency forward contracts are generally short-term in duraïŋ―on and we do not use them for trading purposes. 

Realized gains or losses with respect to our foreign currency exposures, net of gains or losses from our foreign currency forward contracts, and also costs incurred to enter into these foreign currency forward contracts are included in non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net in our consolidated financial statements. Our ulïŋ―mate realized gain or loss with respect to foreign currency exposures will generally depend on the size and type of cross-currency transacïŋ―ons that we enter into, the currency exchange rates associated with these exposures and changes in those rates, the net realized gain or loss on our foreign currency forward contracts and other factors. Furthermore, as a large porïŋ―on of our consolidated operaïŋ―ons are internaïŋ―onal, we could experience addiïŋ―onal foreign currency volaïŋ―lity in the future, in which the amounts and ïŋ―ming are unknown. Refer to Note 1 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements included elsewhere in this Annual Report for addiïŋ―onal details about our foreign currency forward contracts.

## **Evaluaïŋ―on of Disclosure Controls and Procedures** 

As of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K, we carried out an evaluaïŋ―on under the supervision and with the parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on of our Disclosure Commiïŋ―ee and our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer, of the effecïŋ―veness of the design and operaïŋ―on of our disclosure controls and procedures pursuant to Exchange Act Rules 13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e). 

Based on our managementâs evaluaïŋ―on (with the parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on of our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer), as of the end of the period covered by this report, our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer has concluded that our disclosure controls and procedures were effecïŋ―ve as of May 31, 2023 to provide reasonable assurance that informaïŋ―on required to be disclosed by us in reports that we file or submit under the Exchange Act is (i) recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the ïŋ―me periods specified in the SEC rules and forms and (ii) accumulated and communicated to our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer as appropriate to allow ïŋ―mely decisions regarding required disclosure. 

## **Managementâs Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

Our management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng, as such term is defined in Exchange Act Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f). Under the supervision and with the parïŋ―cipaïŋ―on of our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer, we conducted an evaluaïŋ―on of the effecïŋ―veness of our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2023 based on the guidelines established in _Internal ControlâIntegrated Framework_ issued by the Commiïŋ―ee of Sponsoring Organizaïŋ―ons of the Treadway Commissionâs 2013 framework. Our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng includes policies and procedures that provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporïŋ―ng and the preparaïŋ―on of financial statements for external reporïŋ―ng purposes in accordance with U.S. GAAP. 

Based on the results of our evaluaïŋ―on, our management concluded that our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng was effecïŋ―ve as of May 31, 2023. We reviewed the results of managementâs assessment with our Finance and Audit Commiïŋ―ee.

## **Inherent Limitaïŋ―ons on Effecïŋ―veness of Controls** 

Our management, including our Principal Execuïŋ―ve and Financial Officer, believes that our disclosure controls and procedures and internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng are designed to provide reasonable assurance of achieving their objecïŋ―ves and are effecïŋ―ve at the reasonable assurance level. However, our management does not expect that our disclosure controls and procedures or our internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng will prevent all errors and all fraud. A control system, no maïŋ―er how well-conceived and operated, can provide only reasonable, not absolute, assurance that the objecïŋ―ves of the control system are met. Further, the design of a control system must reflect the fact that there are resource constraints and the benefits of controls must be considered relaïŋ―ve to their costs. Because of the inherent limitaïŋ―ons in all control systems, no evaluaïŋ―on of controls can provide absolute assurance that all control issues and instances of fraud, if any, have been detected. These inherent limitaïŋ―ons include the realiïŋ―es that judgments in decision making can be faulty and that breakdowns can occur because of a simple error or mistake. Addiïŋ―onally, controls can be circumvented by the individual acts of some persons, by collusion of two or more people or by management override of the controls. The design of any system of controls also is based in part upon certain assumpïŋ―ons about the likelihood of future events and there can be no assurance that any design will succeed in achieving its stated goals under all potenïŋ―al future condiïŋ―ons; over ïŋ―me, controls may become inadequate because of changes in condiïŋ―ons, or the degree of compliance with policies or procedures may deteriorate. Because of the inherent limitaïŋ―ons in a cost-effecïŋ―ve control system, misstatements due to error or fraud may occur and not be detected.

## **Report of Independent Registered Public Accounïŋ―ng Firm** 

To the Stockholders and the Board of Directors of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on 

## **Opinion on the Financial Statements** 

We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on (the Company) as of May 31, 2023 and 2022, the related consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons, comprehensive income, stockholdersâ equity (deficit) and cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended May 31, 2023, and the related notes (collecïŋ―vely referred to as the âfinancial statementsâ). In our opinion, the financial statements present fairly, in all material respects, the financial posiïŋ―on of the Company at May 31, 2023 and 2022, and the results of its operaïŋ―ons and its cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended May 31, 2023, in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles. 

We also have audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounïŋ―ng Oversight Board (United States) (PCAOB), the Company's internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2023, based on criteria established in Internal Control-Integrated Framework issued by the Commiïŋ―ee of Sponsoring Organizaïŋ―ons of the Treadway Commission (2013 framework) and our report dated June 20, 2023 expressed an unqualified opinion thereon. 

## **Basis for Opinion** 

These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on the Companyâs financial statements based on our audits. We are a public accounïŋ―ng firm registered with the PCAOB and are required to be independent with respect to the Company in accordance with the U.S. federal securiïŋ―es laws and the applicable rules and regulaïŋ―ons of the Securiïŋ―es and Exchange Commission and the PCAOB. 

We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the PCAOB. Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement, whether due to error or fraud. Our audits included performing procedures to assess the risks of material misstatement of the financial statements, whether due to error or fraud, and performing procedures that respond to those risks. Such procedures included examining, on a test basis, evidence regarding the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements. Our audits also included evaluaïŋ―ng the accounïŋ―ng principles used and significant esïŋ―mates made by management, as well as evaluaïŋ―ng the overall presentaïŋ―on of the financial statements. We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.

## **Report of Independent Registered Public Accounïŋ―ng Firm** 

To the Stockholders and the Board of Directors of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on 

## **Opinion on Internal Control Over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

We have audited Oracle Corporaïŋ―onâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2023, based on criteria established in the Internal Controlâ Integrated Framework issued by the Commiïŋ―ee of Sponsoring Organizaïŋ―ons of the Treadway Commission (2013 framework) (the COSO criteria). In our opinion, Oracle Corporaïŋ―on (the Company) maintained, in all material respects, effecïŋ―ve internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng as of May 31, 2023, based on the COSO criteria. 

We also have audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounïŋ―ng Oversight Board (United States) (PCAOB), the consolidated balance sheets of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on as of May 31, 2023 and 2022, the related consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons, comprehensive income, stockholdersâ equity (deficit) and cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended May 31, 2023, and the related notes and our report dated June 20, 2023 expressed an unqualified opinion thereon. 

## **Basis for Opinion** 

The Companyâs management is responsible for maintaining effecïŋ―ve internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng and for its assessment of the effecïŋ―veness of internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng included in the accompanying Managementâs Report on Internal Control Over Financial Reporïŋ―ng. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on the Companyâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng based on our audit. We are a public accounïŋ―ng firm registered with the PCAOB and are required to be independent with respect to the Company in accordance with the U.S. federal securiïŋ―es laws and the applicable rules and regulaïŋ―ons of the Securiïŋ―es and Exchange Commission and the PCAOB. 

We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the PCAOB. Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether effecïŋ―ve internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng was maintained in all material respects. 

Our audit included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists, tesïŋ―ng and evaluaïŋ―ng the design and operaïŋ―ng effecïŋ―veness of internal control based on the assessed risk, and performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis for our opinion. 

## **Definiïŋ―on and Limitaïŋ―ons of Internal Control Over Financial Reporïŋ―ng** 

A companyâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporïŋ―ng and the preparaïŋ―on of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles. A companyâs internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng includes those policies and procedures that (1) pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transacïŋ―ons and disposiïŋ―ons of the assets of the company; (2) provide reasonable assurance that transacïŋ―ons are recorded as necessary to permit preparaïŋ―on of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles, and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizaïŋ―ons of management and directors of the company; and (3) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevenïŋ―on or ïŋ―mely detecïŋ―on of unauthorized acquisiïŋ―on, use, or disposiïŋ―on of the companyâs assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements. 

Because of its inherent limitaïŋ―ons, internal control over financial reporïŋ―ng may not prevent or detect misstatements. Also, projecïŋ―ons of any evaluaïŋ―on of effecïŋ―veness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in condiïŋ―ons, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
