## **1. ORGANIZATION AND SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES** 

Oracle Corporaïŋ―on provides products and services that substanïŋ―ally address all aspects of enterprise informaïŋ―on technology (IT) environments, including applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. We deliver our products and services to customers worldwide through a variety of flexible and interoperable IT deployment models. These models include on-premise, cloud-based and hybrid deployments (an approach that combines both on-premise and cloud based deployments). Oracle Cloud Soïŋ―ware-as-a-Service and Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (SaaS and OCI, respecïŋ―vely, and collecïŋ―vely, Oracle Cloud Services) offerings provide comprehensive and integrated applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure services delivered via various cloud delivery models enabling our customers to choose the best opïŋ―on that meets their specific business needs. Customers may also elect to purchase Oracle soïŋ―ware licenses and hardware products and related services to manage their own cloud-based or on-premise IT environments. Customers that purchase our soïŋ―ware licenses may elect to purchase license support contracts, which provide our customers with rights to unspecified license upgrades and maintenance releases issued during the support period as well as technical support assistance. Customers that purchase our hardware products may elect to purchase hardware support contracts, which provide customers with soïŋ―ware updates and can include product repairs, maintenance services, and technical support services. We also offer customers a broad set of services offerings that are designed to improve customer uïŋ―lizaïŋ―on of their investments in Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. 

Oracle Corporaïŋ―on conducts business globally and was incorporated in 2005 as a Delaware corporaïŋ―on and is the successor to operaïŋ―ons originally begun in June 1977. 

## **Basis of Financial Statements** 

The consolidated financial statements include our accounts and the accounts of our wholly- and majority-owned subsidiaries. Noncontrolling interest posiïŋ―ons of certain of our consolidated enïŋ―ïŋ―es are reported as a separate component of consolidated equity from the equity aïŋ―ributable to Oracleâs stockholders for all periods presented. The noncontrolling interests in our net income were not significant to our consolidated results for the periods presented and therefore have not been presented separately and instead are included as a component of non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. Intercompany transacïŋ―ons and balances have been eliminated. 

On June 8, 2022, we completed our acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner Corporaïŋ―on (Cerner), a provider of digital informaïŋ―on systems used within hospitals and health systems, by means of a merger of one of our wholly owned subsidiaries with and into Cerner such that Cerner became an indirect, wholly owned subsidiary of Oracle. Through our acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner, we enhanced our offerings of each of our three exisïŋ―ng businesses, cloud and license, hardware and services. The consolidated financial statements included in this Annual Report include the financial results of Cerner prospecïŋ―vely from the date of acquisiïŋ―on. Refer to Note 2 below for addiïŋ―onal details regarding our acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner. 

The comparability of our consolidated financial statements as of and for the year ended May 31, 2022 was impacted by $4.7 billion of certain liïŋ―gaïŋ―on related charges during fiscal 2022. The comparability of our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons for the year ended May 31, 2021 was impacted by a $2.3 billion net income tax benefit related to the parïŋ―al realignment of our legal enïŋ―ty structure that resulted in the intra-group transfer of certain intellectual property rights. Refer to Note 13 below for addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on regarding our income taxes.

## **Use of Esïŋ―mates** 

Our consolidated financial statements are prepared in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounïŋ―ng principles (GAAP) as set forth in the Financial Accounïŋ―ng Standards Boardâs (FASB) Accounïŋ―ng Standards Codificaïŋ―on (ASC), and we consider various staff accounïŋ―ng bulleïŋ―ns and other applicable guidance issued by the SEC. These accounïŋ―ng principles require us to make certain esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons. We believe that the esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons upon which we rely are reasonable based upon informaïŋ―on available to us at the ïŋ―me that these esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons are made. These esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons can affect the reported amounts of assets and liabiliïŋ―es as of the date of the financial statements as well as the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the periods presented. To the extent that there are differences between these esïŋ―mates, judgments or assumpïŋ―ons and actual results, our consolidated financial statements will be affected. In many cases, the accounïŋ―ng treatment of a parïŋ―cular transacïŋ―on is specifically dictated by GAAP and does not require managementâs judgment in its applicaïŋ―on. There are also areas in which managementâs judgment in selecïŋ―ng among available alternaïŋ―ves would not produce a materially different result. 

During the first quarter of fiscal 2023, we completed an assessment of the useful lives of our servers and increased the esïŋ―mate of the useful lives from four years to five years effecïŋ―ve at the beginning of fiscal 2023. Based on the carrying value of our servers as of May 31, 2022, this change in accounïŋ―ng esïŋ―mate decreased our total operaïŋ―ng expenses by $434 million during fiscal 2023. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on** 

Our sources of revenues include: 

- cloud and license revenues, which include the sale of: cloud services and license support; and cloud licenses and on-premise licenses, which typically represent perpetual soïŋ―ware licenses purchased by customers for use in both cloud and on-premise IT environments; 

- hardware revenues, which include the sale of hardware products, including Oracle Engineered Systems, servers, and storage products, and industryspecific hardware; and hardware support revenues; and 

- services revenues, which are earned from providing cloud-, license- and hardware-related services including consulïŋ―ng and advanced customer services. 

License support revenues are typically generated through the sale of license support contracts related to cloud license and on-premise licenses purchased by our customers at their opïŋ―on. License support contracts provide customers with rights to unspecified soïŋ―ware product upgrades, maintenance releases and patches released during the term of the support period and include internet access to technical content, as well as internet and telephone access to technical support personnel. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net cloud license and on-premise license fees. Substanïŋ―ally all of our customers elect to purchase and renew their license support contracts annually. 

Cloud services revenues include revenues from Oracle Cloud Services offerings, which deliver applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies via cloud-based deployment models that we develop funcïŋ―onality for, provide unspecified updates and enhancements for, deploy, host, manage, upgrade and support and that customers access by entering into a subscripïŋ―on agreement with us for a stated period. 

Cloud license and on-premise license revenues primarily represent amounts earned from granïŋ―ng customers perpetual licenses to use our database, middleware, applicaïŋ―on and industry-specific soïŋ―ware products, which our customers use for cloud-based, on-premise and other IT environments. The vast majority of our cloud license and on-premise license arrangements include license support contracts, which are entered into at the customerâs opïŋ―on. 

Revenues from the sale of hardware products represent amounts earned primarily from the sale of our Oracle Engineered Systems, computer servers, storage, and industry-specific hardware. Our hardware support offerings generally provide customers with soïŋ―ware updates for the soïŋ―ware components that are essenïŋ―al to the funcïŋ―onality of the hardware products purchased and can also include product repairs, maintenance services and

technical support services. Hardware support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net hardware products fees. 

Our services are offered to customers as standalone arrangements or as a part of arrangements to customers buying other products and services. Our consulïŋ―ng services are designed to help our customers to, among others, deploy, architect, integrate, upgrade and secure their investments in Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. Our advanced customer services are designed to provide supplemental support services, performance services and higher availability for Oracle products and services. 

We apply the provisions of ASC 606, _Revenue from Contracts with Customers_ (ASC 606) as a single standard for revenue recogniïŋ―on that applies to all of our cloud, license, hardware and services arrangements and generally require revenues to be recognized upon the transfer of control of promised goods or services provided to our customers, reflecïŋ―ng the amount of consideraïŋ―on we expect to receive for those goods or services. Pursuant to ASC 606, revenues are recognized upon the applicaïŋ―on of the following steps: 

- idenïŋ―ficaïŋ―on of the contract, or contracts, with a customer; 

- idenïŋ―ficaïŋ―on of the performance obligaïŋ―ons in the contract; 

- determinaïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price; 

- allocaïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price to each performance obligaïŋ―on in the contract; and 

- recogniïŋ―on of revenues when, or as, the contractual performance obligaïŋ―ons are saïŋ―sfied. 

Our customers that contract with us for the provision of cloud services, soïŋ―ware, hardware or other services include businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and our channel partners, which include resellers and system integrators. 

The ïŋ―ming of revenue recogniïŋ―on may differ from the ïŋ―ming of invoicing to our customers. We record an unbilled receivable, which is included within accounts receivable on our consolidated balance sheets, when revenue is recognized prior to invoicing. We record deferred revenues on our consolidated balance sheets when revenues are to be recognized subsequent to cash collecïŋ―on for an invoice. Our standard payment terms are generally net 30 days but may vary. Invoices for cloud license and on-premise licenses and hardware products are generally issued when the license is made available for customer use or upon delivery to the customer of the hardware product. Invoices for license support and hardware support contracts are generally invoiced annually in advance. Cloud SaaS and cloud infrastructure contracts are generally invoiced annually, quarterly or monthly in advance. Services are generally invoiced in advance or as the services are performed. Most contracts that contain a financing component are contracts financed through our Oracle financing division. The transacïŋ―on price for a contract that is financed through our Oracle financing division is adjusted to reflect the ïŋ―me value of money and interest revenue is recorded as a component of non-operaïŋ―ng expenses or income, net within our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons based on market rates in the country in which the transacïŋ―on is being financed. 

Our revenue arrangements generally include standard warranty or service level provisions that our arrangements will perform and operate in all material respects as defined in the respecïŋ―ve agreements, the financial impacts of which have historically been and are expected to conïŋ―nue to be insignificant. Our arrangements generally do not include a general right of return relaïŋ―ve to the delivered products or services. We recognize revenues net of any taxes collected from customers, which are subsequently remiïŋ―ed to governmental authoriïŋ―es. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Cloud Services** 

Revenues from cloud services provided on a subscripïŋ―on basis are generally recognized ratably over the contractual period that the cloud services are delivered, beginning on the date our service is made available to a customer. We recognize revenue ratably because the customer receives and consumes the benefits of the cloud services throughout the contract period. Revenues from cloud services that are provided on a consumpïŋ―on basis, such as metered services, are generally recognized based on the uïŋ―lizaïŋ―on of the services by the customer.

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for License Support and Hardware Support** 

Oracleâs primary performance obligaïŋ―ons with respect to license support contracts and hardware support contracts are to provide customers with technical support as needed and unspecified soïŋ―ware product upgrades, maintenance releases and patches during the term of the support period, if and when they are available, and hardware product repairs, as applicable. Oracle is obligated to make the license and hardware support services available conïŋ―nuously throughout the contract period. Therefore, revenues for license support contracts and hardware support contracts are generally recognized ratably over the contractual periods that the support services are provided. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Cloud Licenses and On-Premise Licenses** 

Revenues from disïŋ―nct cloud license and on-premise license performance obligaïŋ―ons are generally recognized upfront at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the customer to download and use. Revenues from usage-based royalty arrangements for disïŋ―nct cloud licenses and on-premise licenses are recognized at the point in ïŋ―me when the soïŋ―ware end user usage occurs. For usage-based royalty arrangements with a fixed minimum guarantee amount, the minimum amount is generally recognized upfront when the soïŋ―ware is made available to the royalty customer. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Hardware Products** 

The hardware product and related soïŋ―ware, such as an operaïŋ―ng system or firmware, are highly interdependent and interrelated and are accounted for as a combined performance obligaïŋ―on. The revenues for this combined performance obligaïŋ―on are generally recognized at the point in ïŋ―me that the hardware product is delivered and ownership is transferred to the customer. 

## **Revenue Recogniïŋ―on for Services** 

Services revenues are generally recognized over ïŋ―me as the services are performed. Revenues for fixed price services are generally recognized over ïŋ―me applying input methods to esïŋ―mate progress to compleïŋ―on. Revenues for consumpïŋ―on-based services are generally recognized as the services are performed. 

## **Allocaïŋ―on of the Transacïŋ―on Price for Contracts that have Mulïŋ―ple Performance Obligaïŋ―ons** 

Many of our contracts include mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons. Judgment is required in determining whether each performance obligaïŋ―on is disïŋ―nct. Oracle products and services generally do not require a significant amount of integraïŋ―on or interdependency; therefore, our products and services are generally not combined. We allocate the transacïŋ―on price for each contract to each performance obligaïŋ―on based on the relaïŋ―ve standalone selling price (SSP) for each performance obligaïŋ―on within each contract. 

We use judgment in determining the SSP for products and services. For substanïŋ―ally all performance obligaïŋ―ons except cloud licenses and on-premise licenses, we are able to establish the SSP based on the observable prices of products or services sold separately in comparable circumstances to similar customers. We typically establish an SSP range for our products and services which is reassessed on a periodic basis or when facts and circumstances change. Our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses have not historically been sold on a standalone basis, as the vast majority of all customers elect to purchase license support contracts at the ïŋ―me of a cloud license and on-premise license purchase. License support contracts are generally priced as a percentage of the net fees paid by the customer to access the license. We are unable to establish the SSP for our cloud licenses and on-premise licenses based on observable prices given the same products are sold for a broad range of amounts (that is, the selling price is highly variable) and a representaïŋ―ve SSP is not discernible from past transacïŋ―ons or other observable evidence. As a result, the SSP for a cloud license and an on-premise license included in a contract with mulïŋ―ple performance obligaïŋ―ons is generally determined by applying a residual approach whereby all other performance obligaïŋ―ons within a contract are first allocated a porïŋ―on of the transacïŋ―on price based upon their respecïŋ―ve SSPs, with any residual amount of transacïŋ―on price allocated to cloud license and on-premise license revenues.

## **Remaining Performance Obligaïŋ―ons from Customer Contracts** 

Trade receivables, net of allowance for credit losses, and deferred revenues are reported net of related uncollected deferred revenues in our consolidated balance sheets as of May 31, 2023 and 2022. The amount of revenues recognized during the year ended May 31, 2023 and 2022 that were included in the opening deferred revenues balance as of May 31, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely, was approximately $8.3 billion and $8.8 billion. Revenues recognized from performance obligaïŋ―ons saïŋ―sfied in prior periods and impairment losses recognized on our receivables were immaterial during each year ended May 31, 2023, 2022 and 2021. 

Remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons represent contracted revenues that had not yet been recognized, and include deferred revenues; invoices that have been issued to customers but were uncollected and have not been recognized as revenues; and amounts that will be invoiced and recognized as revenues in future periods. The volumes and amounts of customer contracts that we book and total revenues that we recognize are impacted by a variety of seasonal factors. In each fiscal year, the amounts and volumes of contracïŋ―ng acïŋ―vity and our total revenues are typically highest in our fourth fiscal quarter and lowest in our first fiscal quarter. These seasonal impacts influence how our remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons change over ïŋ―me and, combined with foreign exchange rate fluctuaïŋ―ons and other factors, influence the amount of remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons that we report at a point in ïŋ―me. As of May 31, 2023, our remaining performance obligaïŋ―ons were $67.9 billion, approximately 49% of which we expect to recognize as revenues over the next twelve months, 35% over the subsequent month 13 to month 36, and the remainder thereaïŋ―er.

## **Business Combinaïŋ―ons** 

We apply the provisions of ASC 805, _Business Combinaïŋ―ons_ (ASC 805), in accounïŋ―ng for our acquisiïŋ―ons. ASC 805 requires that we evaluate whether a transacïŋ―on pertains to an acquisiïŋ―on of assets, or to an acquisiïŋ―on of a business. A business is defined as an integrated set of assets and acïŋ―viïŋ―es that is capable of being conducted and managed for the purpose of providing a return to investors. Asset acquisiïŋ―ons are accounted for by allocaïŋ―ng the cost of the acquisiïŋ―on to the individual assets and liabiliïŋ―es assumed on a relaïŋ―ve fair value basis; whereas the acquisiïŋ―on of a business requires us to recognize separately from goodwill the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values. Goodwill as of the business acquisiïŋ―on date is measured as the excess of consideraïŋ―on transferred over the net of the acquisiïŋ―on date fair values of the assets acquired and the liabiliïŋ―es assumed. While we use our best esïŋ―mates and assumpïŋ―ons to accurately value assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed at the business acquisiïŋ―on date as well as any conïŋ―ngent consideraïŋ―on, where applicable, our esïŋ―mates are inherently uncertain and subject to refinement. As a result, during the measurement period, which may be up to one year from the business acquisiïŋ―on date, we record adjustments to the assets acquired and liabiliïŋ―es assumed with the corresponding offset to goodwill. Upon the conclusion of a business acquisiïŋ―onâs measurement period or final determinaïŋ―on of the values of assets acquired or liabiliïŋ―es assumed, whichever comes first, any subsequent adjustments are recorded to our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. Costs to exit or restructure certain acïŋ―viïŋ―es of an acquired company or our internal operaïŋ―ons are accounted for as terminaïŋ―on and exit costs pursuant to ASC 420, Exit or Disposal Cost Obligaïŋ―ons, and are accounted for separately from the business combinaïŋ―on. A liability for costs associated with an exit or disposal acïŋ―vity is recognized and measured at its fair value in our consolidated statement of operaïŋ―ons in the period in which the liability is incurred. Abandoned operaïŋ―ng leases related to an acquired company or our internal operaïŋ―ons are accounted for as Right-of-Use (ROU) asset impairment charges pursuant to ASC 842, _Leases_ and are accounted for separately from the business combinaïŋ―on. ## **Marketable and Non-Marketable Investments** 

In accordance with ASC 320, _InvestmentsâDebt Securiïŋ―es_ , and based on our intenïŋ―ons regarding these instruments, we classify substanïŋ―ally all of our marketable debt securiïŋ―es investments as available-for-sale. Investments in equity securiïŋ―es, other than any equity method investments, are generally recorded at their fair values, if the fair values are readily determinable. ## **Fair Values of Financial Instruments** 

We apply the provisions of ASC 820, _Fair Value Measurement_ (ASC 820), to our assets and liabiliïŋ―es that we are required to measure at fair value pursuant to other accounïŋ―ng standards, including our investments in marketable debt and equity securiïŋ―es and our derivaïŋ―ve financial instruments.

## **Allowances for Credit Losses** 

We record allowances for credit losses based upon a specific review of all significant outstanding invoices. For those invoices not specifically reviewed, provisions are provided at differing rates, based upon the age of the receivable, the collecïŋ―on history associated with the geographic region that the receivable was recorded in and current and expected future economic condiïŋ―ons. We write-off a receivable and charge it against its recorded allowance when we have exhausted our collecïŋ―on efforts without success. 

## **Concentraïŋ―ons of Credit Risk** 

Financial instruments that are potenïŋ―ally subject to concentraïŋ―ons of credit risk consist primarily of cash and cash equivalents, marketable securiïŋ―es, derivaïŋ―ves and trade receivables. Our cash and cash equivalents are generally held with large, diverse financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons worldwide to reduce the amount of exposure to any single financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―on. Investment policies have been implemented that limit purchases of marketable debt securiïŋ―es to investment-grade securiïŋ―es. Our derivaïŋ―ve contracts are transacted with various financial insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons with high credit standings and any exposure to counterparty credit-related losses in these contracts is largely miïŋ―gated with collateral security agreements that provide for collateral to be received or posted when the net fair values of these contracts fluctuate from contractually established thresholds. We generally do not require collateral to secure accounts receivable. The risk with respect to trade receivables is miïŋ―gated by credit evaluaïŋ―ons we perform on our customers, the short duraïŋ―on of our payment terms for the significant majority of our customer contracts and by the diversificaïŋ―on of our customer base. No single customer accounted for 10% or more of our total revenues in fiscal 2023, 2022 or 2021. 

We outsource the manufacturing, assembly and delivery of the substanïŋ―al majority of our hardware products to a variety of companies, many of which are located outside the U.S. Further, we have simplified our supply chain processes by reducing the number of third-party manufacturing partners and the number of locaïŋ―ons where these third-party manufacturers build our hardware products. Any inability of these third-party manufacturing partners to deliver the contracted services for our hardware products could adversely impact future operaïŋ―ng results of our cloud and license and hardware businesses. 

## **Inventories** 

Inventories are stated at the lower of cost or net realizable value. Cost is computed using standard cost, which approximates actual cost, on a first-in, first-out basis. We evaluate our ending inventories for esïŋ―mated excess quanïŋ―ïŋ―es and obsolescence. This evaluaïŋ―on includes analysis of sales levels by product and projecïŋ―ons of future demand within specific ïŋ―me horizons. Inventories in excess of future demand are wriïŋ―en down and charged to hardware expenses. In addiïŋ―on, we assess the impact of changing technology to our inventories and we write down inventories that are considered obsolete. At the point of loss recogniïŋ―on, a new, lower-cost basis for that inventory is established, and subsequent changes in facts and circumstances do not result in the restoraïŋ―on or increase in that newly established cost basis. Inventories are included in prepaid expenses and other current assets in our consolidated balance sheets and totaled $298 million and $314 million at May 31, 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely. 

## **Other Receivables** 

Other receivables represent value-added tax and sales tax receivables associated with the sale of our products and services to third parïŋ―es. Other receivables are included in prepaid expenses and other current assets in our consolidated balance sheets and totaled $798 million and $791 million at May 31, 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely.

## **Deferred Sales Commissions** 

We defer sales commissions earned by our sales force that are considered to be incremental and recoverable costs of obtaining a cloud, license support and hardware support contract. Iniïŋ―al sales commissions for the majority of these aforemenïŋ―oned contracts are generally deferred and amorïŋ―zed on a straight-line basis over a period of benefit that we esïŋ―mate to be four years. We determine the period of benefit by taking into consideraïŋ―on the historical and expected duraïŋ―ons of our customer contracts, the expected useful lives of our technologies, and other factors. Sales commissions for renewal contracts relaïŋ―ng to certain of our cloud-based arrangements are generally deferred and then amorïŋ―zed on a straight-line basis over the related contractual renewal period, which is generally one to three years. Amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on of deferred sales commissions is included as a component of sales and markeïŋ―ng expenses in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons and asset balances for deferred sales commissions are included in other current assets and other non-current assets in our consolidated balance sheets. 

## **Property, Plant and Equipment** 

Property, plant and equipment are stated at cost, less accumulated depreciaïŋ―on. Depreciaïŋ―on is computed using the straight-line method based on esïŋ―mated useful lives of the assets, which range from one to 40 years. Leasehold improvements are amorïŋ―zed over the lesser of the esïŋ―mated useful lives of the improvements or the lease terms, as appropriate. Property, plant and equipment are periodically reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable. We did not recognize any significant property impairment charges in fiscal 2023, 2022 or 2021. 

## **Goodwill, Intangible Assets and Impairment Assessments** 

Goodwill represents the excess of the purchase price in a business combinaïŋ―on over the fair value of net tangible and intangible assets acquired. Intangible assets that are not considered to have an indefinite useful life are itemized in Note 6 below and are amorïŋ―zed over their useful lives, which generally range from one to 10 years. Each period we evaluate the esïŋ―mated remaining useful lives of purchased intangible assets and whether events or changes in circumstances warrant a revision to the remaining periods of amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on. 

The carrying amounts of our goodwill and intangible assets are periodically reviewed for impairment (at least annually for goodwill and indefinite lived intangible assets) and whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying value of these assets may not be recoverable. When goodwill is assessed for impairment, we have the opïŋ―on to perform an assessment of qualitaïŋ―ve factors of impairment (opïŋ―onal assessment) prior to necessitaïŋ―ng a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve impairment test. Should the opïŋ―onal assessment be used for any given fiscal year, qualitaïŋ―ve factors considered for a reporïŋ―ng unit include: cost factors; financial performance; legal, regulatory, contractual, poliïŋ―cal, business, or other factors; enïŋ―ty specific factors; industry and market consideraïŋ―ons; macroeconomic condiïŋ―ons; and other relevant events and factors affecïŋ―ng the reporïŋ―ng unit. If we determine in the qualitaïŋ―ve assessment that it is more likely than not that the fair value of the reporïŋ―ng unit is less than its carrying value, a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve test is then performed. Otherwise, no further tesïŋ―ng is required. For those reporïŋ―ng units tested using a quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve approach, we compare the fair value of each reporïŋ―ng unit with the carrying amount of the reporïŋ―ng unit, including goodwill. To determine the fair value of each reporïŋ―ng unit we uïŋ―lize esïŋ―mates, judgments and assumpïŋ―ons including esïŋ―mated future cash flows the reporïŋ―ng unit is expected to generate on a discounted basis; the discount rate used as a part of the discounted cash flow analysis; future economic and market condiïŋ―ons; and market comparables of peer companies, among others. If, as per the quanïŋ―taïŋ―ve test, the esïŋ―mated fair value of the reporïŋ―ng unit is less than the carrying amount of the reporïŋ―ng unit, impairment is recognized for the difference, limited to the amount of goodwill recognized for the reporïŋ―ng unit. Our most recent goodwill impairment analysis was performed on March 1, 2023 and did not result in a goodwill impairment charge. We did not recognize impairment charges in fiscal 2022 or 2021. 

76 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

Recoverability of finite lived intangible assets is measured by comparison of the carrying amount of the asset to the future undiscounted cash flows that are expected to be generated by the lowest level associated asset grouping. Recoverability of indefinite lived intangible assets is measured by comparison of the carrying amount of the asset to its fair value. If the asset is considered to be impaired, the amount of any impairment is measured as the difference between the carrying value and the fair value of the impaired asset. We did not recognize any intangible asset impairment charges in fiscal 2023, 2022 or 2021. At least annually, we assess the useful lives of our finite lived intangible assets and may adjust the period over which these assets are amorïŋ―zed whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that a shorter amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on period is more reflecïŋ―ve of the period in which these assets contribute to our cash flows. 

## **Derivaïŋ―ve Financial Instruments** 

During fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, we used derivaïŋ―ve financial instruments to manage foreign currency and interest rate risks. We do not use derivaïŋ―ve financial instruments for trading purposes. We account for these instruments in accordance with ASC 815, _Derivaïŋ―ves and Hedging_ (ASC 815), which requires that every derivaïŋ―ve instrument be recorded on the balance sheet as either an asset or liability measured at its fair value as of each reporïŋ―ng date. ASC 815 also requires that changes in our derivaïŋ―vesâ fair values be recognized in earnings, unless specific hedge accounïŋ―ng and documentaïŋ―on criteria are met (i.e., the instruments are accounted for as hedges). 

The accounïŋ―ng for changes in the fair value of a derivaïŋ―ve depends on the intended use of the derivaïŋ―ve and the resulïŋ―ng designaïŋ―on. For a derivaïŋ―ve instrument designated as a fair value hedge, loss or gain aïŋ―ributable to the risk being hedged is recognized in earnings in the period of change with a corresponding earnings offset recorded to the item for which the risk is being hedged. For a derivaïŋ―ve instrument designated as a cash flow hedge, during each reporïŋ―ng period, we record the change in fair value of the derivaïŋ―ve to accumulated other comprehensive loss (AOCL) in our consolidated balance sheets and the change is reclassified to earnings in the period the hedged item affects earnings. 

## **Leases** 

We determine if an arrangement is a lease at its incepïŋ―on. Operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es are recognized at the lease commencement date based on the present value of lease payments over the lease term. We generally use our incremental borrowing rate based on the informaïŋ―on available at the lease commencement date in determining the present value of future payments, because the implicit rate of the lease is generally not known. ROU assets related to our operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es are measured at lease incepïŋ―on based on the iniïŋ―al measurement of the lease liability, plus any prepaid lease payments and less any lease incenïŋ―ves. Our lease terms that are used in determining our operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es at lease incepïŋ―on may include opïŋ―ons to extend or terminate the leases when it is reasonably certain that we will exercise such opïŋ―ons. We amorïŋ―ze our ROU assets as operaïŋ―ng lease expense generally on a straight-line basis over the lease term and classify both the lease amorïŋ―zaïŋ―on and imputed interest as operaïŋ―ng expenses. We have lease agreements with lease and non-lease components, and in such cases, we generally account for the components as a single lease component. We do not recognize lease assets and lease liabiliïŋ―es for any lease with an original lease term of less than one year. 

ROU assets related to our operaïŋ―ng leases are included in other non-current assets, short-term operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es are included in other current liabiliïŋ―es, and long-term operaïŋ―ng lease liabiliïŋ―es are included in other non-current liabiliïŋ―es in our consolidated balance sheets. Cash flow movements related to our lease acïŋ―viïŋ―es are included in prepaid expenses and other assets and accounts payable and other liabiliïŋ―es as presented in net cash provided by operaïŋ―ng acïŋ―viïŋ―es in our consolidated statements of cash flows for the years ended May 31, 2023 and 2022. Note 10 below provides addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on regarding our leases.

## **Foreign Currency** 

We transact business in various foreign currencies. In general, the funcïŋ―onal currency of a foreign operaïŋ―on is the local countryâs currency. Consequently, revenues and expenses of operaïŋ―ons outside the U.S. are translated into U.S. Dollars using weighted-average exchange rates while assets and liabiliïŋ―es of operaïŋ―ons outside the U.S. are translated into U.S. Dollars using exchange rates at the balance sheet dates. The effects of foreign currency translaïŋ―on adjustments are substanïŋ―ally included in stockholdersâ equity as a component of AOCL in the accompanying consolidated balance sheets and related periodic movements are summarized as a line item in our consolidated statements of comprehensive income. ## **Stock-Based Compensaïŋ―on** 

We account for share-based payments to employees, including grants of service-based restricted stock unit awards, service-based employee stock opïŋ―ons, performance-based stock opïŋ―ons (PSOs), and purchases under employee stock purchase plans in accordance with ASC 718, _Compensaïŋ―on_ â _Stock Compensaïŋ―on,_ which requires that share-based payments (to the extent they are compensatory) be recognized in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons based on their fair values. We account for forfeitures of stock-based awards as they occur. 

For our service-based stock awards, we recognize stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense on a straight-line basis over the service period of the award, which is generally four years. 

For our PSOs, we recognize stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense on a straight-line basis related to awards that are probable of achievement over the longer of the (a) esïŋ―mated implicit service period for performance-metric achievement, or (b) derived service period for market-based metric achievement. During our interim and annual reporïŋ―ng periods, stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense is recorded based on expected aïŋ―ainment of performance targets. Changes in our esïŋ―mates of the expected aïŋ―ainment of performance targets that result in a change in the number of shares that are expected to vest, or changes in our esïŋ―mates of implicit service periods, may cause the amount of stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense that we record for each interim reporïŋ―ng period to vary. Any changes in esïŋ―mates that impact our expectaïŋ―on of the number of shares that are expected to vest are reflected in the amount of stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense that we recognize for each PSO tranche on a cumulaïŋ―ve catch up basis during each interim reporïŋ―ng period in which such esïŋ―mates are altered. Changes in esïŋ―mates of the implicit service periods are recognized prospecïŋ―vely. 

We record deferred tax assets for stock-based compensaïŋ―on awards that result in deducïŋ―ons on certain of our income tax returns based on the amount of stock-based compensaïŋ―on recognized in each reporïŋ―ng period and the fair values aïŋ―ributable to the vested porïŋ―on of stock awards assumed in connecïŋ―on with a business combinaïŋ―on at the statutory tax rates in the jurisdicïŋ―ons that we are able to recognize such tax deducïŋ―ons. The impacts of the actual tax deducïŋ―ons for stock-based awards that are realized in these jurisdicïŋ―ons are generally recognized in the reporïŋ―ng period that a restricted stock-based award vests or a stock opïŋ―on is exercised with any shorïŋ―all/windfall relaïŋ―ve to the deferred tax asset established, and recorded as a discrete detriment/benefit to our provision for income taxes in such period. Note 12 below provides addiïŋ―onal informaïŋ―on regarding our stock-based compensaïŋ―on plans and related expenses.

## **Income Taxes** 

We account for income taxes in accordance with ASC 740, _Income Taxes_ (ASC 740). Deferred income taxes are recorded for the expected tax consequences of temporary differences between the tax bases of assets and liabiliïŋ―es for financial reporïŋ―ng purposes and amounts recognized for income tax purposes. We record a valuaïŋ―on allowance to reduce our deferred tax assets to the amount of future tax benefit that is more likely than not to be realized. 

A two-step approach is applied pursuant to ASC 740 in the recogniïŋ―on and measurement of uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. The first step is to determine if the weight of available evidence indicates that it is more likely than not that the tax posiïŋ―on will be sustained in an audit, including resoluïŋ―on of any related appeals or liïŋ―gaïŋ―on processes. The second step is to measure the tax benefit as the largest amount that is more than 50% likely to be realized upon ulïŋ―mate seïŋ―lement. We recognize interest and penalïŋ―es related to uncertain tax posiïŋ―ons in our provision for income taxes line of our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons. 

A descripïŋ―on of our accounïŋ―ng policies associated with tax related conïŋ―ngencies and valuaïŋ―on allowances assumed as a part of a business combinaïŋ―on is provided under âBusiness Combinaïŋ―onsâ above.

Vested equity awards outstanding immediately prior to the consummaïŋ―on of the merger were cancelled in exchange for the right to receive an amount in cash based on a formula contained in the Merger Agreement. ## **4. FAIR VALUE MEASUREMENTS** 

We perform fair value measurements in accordance with ASC 820. ASC 820 defines fair value as the price that would be received from selling an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transacïŋ―on between market parïŋ―cipants at the measurement date. When determining the fair value measurements for assets and liabiliïŋ―es required to be recorded at their fair values, we consider the principal or most advantageous market in which we would transact and consider assumpïŋ―ons that market parïŋ―cipants would use when pricing the assets or liabiliïŋ―es, such as inherent risk, transfer restricïŋ―ons and risk of nonperformance. 

ASC 820 establishes a fair value hierarchy that requires an enïŋ―ty to maximize the use of observable inputs and minimize the use of unobservable inputs when measuring fair value. An assetâs or a liabilityâs categorizaïŋ―on within the fair value hierarchy is based upon the lowest level of input that is significant to the fair value measurement. ASC 820 establishes three levels of inputs that may be used to measure fair value: 

- Level 1: quoted prices in acïŋ―ve markets for idenïŋ―cal assets or liabiliïŋ―es; 

- Level 2: inputs other than Level 1 that are observable, either directly or indirectly, such as quoted prices in acïŋ―ve markets for similar assets or liabiliïŋ―es, quoted prices for idenïŋ―cal or similar assets or liabiliïŋ―es in markets that are not acïŋ―ve, or other inputs that are observable or can be corroborated by observable market data for substanïŋ―ally the full term of the assets or liabiliïŋ―es; or 

- Level 3: unobservable inputs that are supported by liïŋ―le or no market acïŋ―vity and that are significant to the fair values of the assets or liabiliïŋ―es.

## **Senior Notes** 

Interest is payable semi-annually for the senior notes listed in the above table except for the Euro Notes for which interest is payable annually. The senior notes rank pari passu with any other notes we may issue in the future pursuant to our commercial paper program (see addiïŋ―onal discussion regarding our commercial paper program below) and all exisïŋ―ng and future unsecured senior indebtedness of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on, including the Revolving Credit Agreement and the Term Loan Credit Agreement as described further below. All exisïŋ―ng and future liabiliïŋ―es of the subsidiaries of Oracle Corporaïŋ―on are or will be effecïŋ―vely senior to the senior notes, borrowings under the Term Loan Credit Agreement, any future borrowings pursuant to the Revolving Credit Agreement and any future issuances of commercial paper notes. We were in compliance with all debt-related covenants at May 31, 2023. 

## **Delayed Draw Term Loan Credit Agreement** 

On June 8, 2022, we borrowed $15.7 billion under a delayed draw term loan credit agreement (Bridge Credit Agreement) that we entered into in March 2022 to partly finance our acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner. The Bridge Credit Agreement provided that, subject to certain excepïŋ―ons, net cash proceeds received by us from certain debt and equity issuances shall result in mandatory prepayments under the Bridge Credit Agreement. Interest was based on either (a) a Term Secured Overnight Financing Rate (SOFR)-based formula plus a margin of 100.0 basis points to 137.5 basis points, depending on the credit raïŋ―ng assigned to our longterm senior unsecured debt, or (b) a Base Rate formula plus a margin of 0.0 basis points to 37.5 basis points, depending on the same such credit raïŋ―ng, each as set forth in the Bridge Credit Agreement. The effecïŋ―ve interest rate for fiscal 2023 was 3.57%. We fully repaid the amount borrowed under the Bridge Credit Agreement during fiscal 2023. 

## **Revolving Credit Agreement** 

Our Revolving Credit Agreement provides for an unsecured $6.0 billion, five-year revolving credit facility (the Revolving Facility) to be used for our working capital purposes and for other general corporate purposes. Subject to certain condiïŋ―ons stated in the Revolving Credit Agreement, we may borrow, prepay and reborrow amounts under the Revolving Facility during the term of the Revolving Credit Agreement. All amounts borrowed under the Revolving Credit Agreement will become due on March 8, 2027, unless the commitments are terminated earlier either at our request or, if an event of default occurs, by the lenders (or automaïŋ―cally in the case of certain bankruptcy-related 

86 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

events). Interest is based on either (a) a Term SOFR-based formula plus a margin of 87.5 basis points to 150.0 basis points, depending on the credit raïŋ―ng assigned to our long-term senior unsecured debt, or (b) a Base Rate formula plus a margin of 0.0 basis points to 50.0 basis points, depending on the same such credit raïŋ―ng, each as set forth in the Revolving Credit Agreement. As of May 31, 2023 and 2022, we did not have any outstanding borrowing under the Revolving Credit Agreement. 

## **Five-Year Term Loan Credit Agreement** 

On August 16, 2022, we entered into a $4.4 billion term loan credit agreement (Term Loan Credit Agreement), which provides for a total term loan commitment of $4.4 billion, comprised of a $3.6 billion term loan (Term Loan 1 Facility) and a $790 million term loan (Term Loan 2 Facility and, together with the Term Loan 1 Facility, the Term Loan Faciliïŋ―es). The proceeds of the Term Loan Faciliïŋ―es may only be used to refinance indebtedness incurred under the Bridge Credit Agreement and to pay related fees and expenses. 

On November 2, 2022, the total term loan commitment was increased by $1.3 billion, comprised of $1.1 billion under the Term Loan 1 Facility and $170 million under the Term Loan 2 Facility pursuant to the terms of the Term Loan Credit Agreement. 

We may request addiïŋ―onal commitments under the Term Loan Credit Agreement up to a maximum of $6.0 billion (each, an Incremental Borrowing). The use of proceeds of any Incremental Borrowing will be specified at the ïŋ―me of such borrowing and may include working capital purposes and other general corporate purposes. 

We iniïŋ―ally borrowed $4.4 billion on August 16, 2022, and we borrowed an incremental $1.3 billion on November 2, 2022, each under the Term Loan Faciliïŋ―es. We used the net proceeds of the borrowings under the Term Loan Credit Agreement to reduce the amount of indebtedness outstanding under the Bridge Credit Agreement. The effecïŋ―ve interest rate for these borrowings during fiscal 2023 was 5.76%. 

The Term Loan Credit Agreement provides for repayment of borrowings under the Term Loan Faciliïŋ―es as follows: 

- an amount equal to the amount borrowed reduced by any prepayments mulïŋ―plied by 1.25% on September 30, 2024 and quarterly thereaïŋ―er unïŋ―l June 30, 2026; 

- an amount equal to the amount borrowed reduced by any prepayments mulïŋ―plied by 2.50% on September 30, 2026 and quarterly thereaïŋ―er unïŋ―l June 30, 2027; and 

- any remaining unpaid principal balance under the Term Loan 1 Facility will become fully due and payable on August 16, 2027 and any remaining unpaid principal balance under the Term Loan 2 Facility will become fully due and payable on August 16, 2025 (subject to any extension of the Term Loan 2 Facility terminaïŋ―on date, as set out below), unless the outstanding loans are prepaid earlier at the request of Oracle or accelerated by the lenders if an event of default occurs. 

The terminaïŋ―on date of the Term Loan 2 Facility may be extended at our sole opïŋ―on by up to 2 years. The terminaïŋ―on date of each Term Loan Facility may also be further extended at each lenderâs opïŋ―on by up to 2 years. 

Interest is based on either (a) a Term SOFR-based formula plus a margin of 147.5 basis points to 197.5 basis points, depending on the credit raïŋ―ng assigned to our long-term senior unsecured debt, or (b) a Base Rate formula plus a margin of 47.5 basis points to 97.5 basis points, depending on the same such credit raïŋ―ng, each as set forth in the Term Loan Credit Agreement. 

The Term Loan Credit Agreement contains certain customary representaïŋ―ons and warranïŋ―es, covenants and events of default, including the requirement that the raïŋ―o of âConsolidated EBITDAâ to âConsolidated Net Interest Expenseâ (each term as defined in the Term Loan Credit Agreement) of Oracle and its subsidiaries shall not be less than 3.0 to 1.0 at the end of any fiscal quarter during the period that the Term Loan Credit Agreement is effecïŋ―ve. If an event of default occurs under the Term Loan Credit Agreement and is not cured within the applicable grace period or waived, any unpaid amounts under the Term Loan Credit Agreement may be declared immediately due and payable. We were in compliance with such covenants as of May 31, 2023.

## **Cash Flow HedgeâInterest Rate Swap Agreements** 

In August 2022, we entered into certain interest rate swap agreements to manage the related interest rate risk of $4.4 billion borrowings under the Term Loan Credit Agreement by effecïŋ―vely converïŋ―ng the floaïŋ―ng-rate to fixed-rate. The economic effect of the swap agreements was to eliminate the uncertainty of the cash flows associated with floaïŋ―ng-rate interest payments of the Term Loan Credit Agreement by a fixed annual interest rate of 3.07%, plus a margin depending on the credit raïŋ―ng assigned to our long-term senior unsecured debt as menïŋ―oned above. We have designated these interest rate swap agreements as qualifying hedging instruments and are accounïŋ―ng for these as cash flow hedges pursuant to ASC 815, _Derivaïŋ―ves and Hedging_ . 

The fair values of these interest rate swap agreements are recognized either as non-current assets or non-current liabiliïŋ―es in our consolidated balance sheets. Changes in the fair values of these interest rate swap agreements are reported in accumulated other comprehensive loss in our consolidated balance sheets and an amount is reclassified out of accumulated other comprehensive loss into non-operaïŋ―ng income or expense, net in the same period that corresponding interest expense is recognized. 

We do not use any interest rate swap agreements for trading purposes. 

## **Cerner Senior Notes and Other Borrowings** 

In connecïŋ―on with our acquisiïŋ―on of Cerner, we assumed: 

- $1.0 billion par value of legacy Cerner senior notes. The acquisiïŋ―on triggered a mandatory offer to prepay such senior notes in accordance with the terms of the underlying note purchase agreements. Holders of $931 million par value of senior notes exercised the opïŋ―on for prepayment, and accordingly, such notes together with accrued interest were redeemed on June 8, 2022, and the remaining outstanding senior notes together with accrued interest were redeemed during the second quarter of fiscal 2023; and 

- $600 million of principal amount of revolving credit loans. The enïŋ―re loan along with accrued interest was seïŋ―led and the credit facility was terminated on June 8, 2022. 

## **Commercial Paper Program and Commercial Paper Notes** 

During the first quarter of fiscal 2023, our commercial paper program was increased to $6.0 billion. Our commercial paper program allows us to issue and sell unsecured short-term promissory notes pursuant to a private placement exempïŋ―on from the registraïŋ―on requirements under federal and state securiïŋ―es laws pursuant to dealer agreements with various banks and an Issuing and Paying Agency Agreement with Deutsche Bank Trust Company Americas. 

There were $563 million of outstanding commercial paper notes as of May 31, 2023 (none outstanding as of May 31, 2022) that mature at various dates through June 2023. The effecïŋ―ve interest rate including issuance costs was 4.89% for fiscal 2023. We use the net proceeds from the issuance of commercial paper for general corporate purposes.

In fiscal 2023, our management supplemented the 2022 Restructuring Plan to reflect addiïŋ―onal acïŋ―ons that we expected to take. Restructuring costs associated with the 2022 Restructuring Plan were recorded to the restructuring expense line item within our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons as they were incurred. We recorded $493 million and $223 million of restructuring expenses in connecïŋ―on with the 2022 Restructuring Plan in

fiscal 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely. The total costs recorded to date in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons in connecïŋ―on with the 2022 Restructuring Plan were $716 million. Acïŋ―ons pursuant to the 2022 Restructuring Plan were substanïŋ―ally complete as of May 31, 2023. 

## **Fiscal 2019 Oracle Restructuring Plan** 

During fiscal 2019, our management approved, commiïŋ―ed to and iniïŋ―ated plans to restructure and further improve efficiencies in our operaïŋ―ons due to our acquisiïŋ―ons and certain other operaïŋ―onal acïŋ―viïŋ―es (2019 Restructuring Plan). In fiscal 2021, our management supplemented the 2019 Restructuring Plan to reflect addiïŋ―onal acïŋ―ons that we expected to take. Restructuring costs associated with the 2019 Restructuring Plan were recorded to the restructuring expense line item within our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons as they were incurred. We recorded $430 million of restructuring expenses in connecïŋ―on with the 2019 Restructuring Plan in fiscal 2021. The total costs recorded in our consolidated statements of operaïŋ―ons in connecïŋ―on with the 2019 Restructuring Plan were $1.2 billion. Acïŋ―ons pursuant to the 2019 Restructuring Plan were substanïŋ―ally complete as of May 31, 2021.

In the ordinary course of business, we enter into certain uncondiïŋ―onal purchase obligaïŋ―ons with our suppliers, which are agreements that are enforceable and legally binding and specify terms, including: fixed or minimum quanïŋ―ïŋ―es to be purchased; fixed, minimum or variable price provisions; and the approximate ïŋ―ming of the payment. We uïŋ―lize several external manufacturers to manufacture sub-assemblies, perform final assemblies and perform tesïŋ―ng of our hardware products. We also obtain individual components for our hardware products from a variety of individual suppliers based on projected demand informaïŋ―on. Such purchase commitments are based on our forecasted component and manufacturing requirements and typically provide for fulfillment within agreed upon lead-ïŋ―mes and/or commercially standard lead-ïŋ―mes for the parïŋ―cular part or product and have been included in the amounts disclosed below. Certain rouïŋ―ne arrangements for other materials and goods that are not related to our external manufacturers and certain other suppliers and that are entered into in the ordinary course of business are not included in the amounts below, as they are generally entered into in order to secure pricing or other negoïŋ―ated terms and are difficult to quanïŋ―fy in a meaningful way.

## **Guarantees** 

Our cloud, license and hardware sales agreements generally include certain provisions for indemnifying customers against liabiliïŋ―es if our products infringe a third partyâs intellectual property rights. To date, we have not incurred 

91 

Table of Contents

any material costs as a result of such indemnificaïŋ―ons and have not accrued any material liabiliïŋ―es related to such obligaïŋ―ons in our consolidated financial statements. Certain of our sales agreements also include provisions indemnifying customers against liabiliïŋ―es in the event we breach confidenïŋ―ality or service level requirements. It is not possible to determine the maximum potenïŋ―al amount under these indemnificaïŋ―on agreements due to our limited and infrequent history of prior indemnificaïŋ―on claims and the unique facts and circumstances involved in each parïŋ―cular agreement. 

Our Oracle Cloud Services agreements generally include a warranty that the cloud services will be performed in all material respects as defined in the agreement during the service period. Our license and hardware agreements also generally include a warranty that our products will substanïŋ―ally operate as described in the applicable program documentaïŋ―on for a period of one year aïŋ―er delivery. We also warrant that services we perform will be provided in a manner consistent with industry standards for a period of 90 days from performance of the services. 

We occasionally are required, for various reasons, to enter into financial guarantees with third parïŋ―es in the ordinary course of our business including, among others, guarantees related to taxes, import licenses and leïŋ―ers of credit on behalf of parïŋ―es with whom we conduct business. Such agreements have not had a material effect on our results of operaïŋ―ons, financial posiïŋ―on or cash flows. 

## **11. STOCKHOLDERSâ EQUITY (DEFICIT)** 

## **Common Stock Repurchases** 

Our Board of Directors has approved a program for us to repurchase shares of our common stock. As of May 31, 2023, approximately $8.2 billion remained available for stock repurchases pursuant to our stock repurchase program. We repurchased 17.0 million shares for $1.3 billion, 185.8 million shares for $16.2 billion, and 329.2 million shares for $21.0 billion in fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely, under the stock repurchase program. 

Our stock repurchase authorizaïŋ―on does not have an expiraïŋ―on date and the pace of our repurchase acïŋ―vity will depend on factors such as our working capital needs, our cash requirements for acquisiïŋ―ons and dividend payments, our debt repayment obligaïŋ―ons or repurchases of our debt, our stock price, and economic and market condiïŋ―ons. Our stock repurchases may be effected from ïŋ―me to ïŋ―me through open market purchases or pursuant to a Rule 10b5-1 trading plan. Our stock repurchase program may be accelerated, suspended, delayed or disconïŋ―nued at any ïŋ―me. 

## **Dividends on Common Stock** 

During fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, our Board of Directors declared cash dividends of $1.36, $1.28 and $1.04 per share of our outstanding common stock, respecïŋ―vely, which we paid during the same period. 

In June 2023, our Board of Directors declared a quarterly cash dividend of $0.40 per share of our outstanding common stock. The dividend is payable on July 26, 2023 to stockholders of record as of the close of business on July 12, 2023. Future declaraïŋ―ons of dividends and the establishment of future record and payment dates are subject to the final determinaïŋ―on of our Board of Directors.

## **12. EMPLOYEE BENEFIT PLANS** 

## **Stock-Based Compensaïŋ―on Plans** 

## **Stock Plans** 

In fiscal 2021, we adopted the 2020 Equity Incenïŋ―ve Plan to replace the Amended and Restated 2000 Long-Term Equity Incenïŋ―ve Plan (the 2000 Plan) which provides for the issuance of long-term performance awards, including restricted stock-based awards, non-qualified stock opïŋ―ons and incenïŋ―ve stock opïŋ―ons, as well as stock purchase rights and stock appreciaïŋ―on rights, to our eligible employees, officers and directors who are also employees or consultants, independent consultants and advisers. In fiscal 2022, our stockholders, upon the recommendaïŋ―on of our Board of Directors (the Board), approved the adopïŋ―on of the Amended and Restated 2020 Equity Incenïŋ―ve Plan (the 2020 Plan and, together with the 2000 Plan, the Plans), which increased the number of authorized shares of stock that may be issued under the 2020 Plan by 300 million shares. 

The total number of shares authorized under the 2020 Plan is (i) 390,000,000 shares, plus (ii) 132,921,827 shares, which were the number of shares that were unissued and available for grant under the 2000 Plan as of the date that the 2020 Plan was originally adopted, plus (iii) the number of shares granted and outstanding as of the date that the 2020 Plan was originally adopted which would have been available again for issuance under the terms of the 2000 Plan had the 2020 Plan not been adopted. Under the 2020 Plan, for each share granted as a full value award in the form of a restricted stock unit (RSU) or a performance-based restricted stock award (PSU), an equivalent of 2.5 shares is deducted from our pool of shares available for grant. 

As of May 31, 2023, 146 million unvested RSUs, 36 million performance-based stock opïŋ―ons (PSOs), of which 6 million shares were vested, and service-based stock opïŋ―ons (SOs) to purchase 28 million shares of common stock, substanïŋ―ally all of which were vested, were outstanding under the Plans. Approximately 208 million shares of common stock were available for future awards under the 2020 Plan as of May 31, 2023. To date, we have not issued any stock opïŋ―ons under the 2020 Plan or any stock purchase rights or stock appreciaïŋ―on rights under either of the Plans. 

The vesïŋ―ng schedule for all awards granted under the Plans is established by the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board. RSUs generally require service-based vesïŋ―ng of 25% annually over four years. SOs were previously granted under the 2000 Plan at not less than fair market value, become exercisable generally 25% annually over four years of service, and generally expire 10 years from the date of grant. 

PSOs granted under the 2000 Plan to our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer and Chief Technology Officer in fiscal 2018 consisted of seven numerically equivalent vesïŋ―ng tranches that potenïŋ―ally could vest. One tranche, which was based solely on the aïŋ―ainment of a market-based metric, was achieved and vested in fiscal 2022. Each of the remaining six tranches requires the aïŋ―ainment of both a performance metric and a market capitalizaïŋ―on metric by May 31, 2022, which was subsequently extended by three addiïŋ―onal fiscal years to May 31, 2025 via an amendment approved by the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board during fiscal 2022. If any of the remaining operaïŋ―onal and market capitalizaïŋ―on performance goals are achieved before May 31, 2025 addiïŋ―onal tranches may vest, assuming conïŋ―nued employment and service through the date the Compensaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee of the Board cerïŋ―fies that performance has been achieved. Upon amendment of the PSOs in fiscal 2022, we esïŋ―mated the revised fair values of the six unvested tranches of the PSOs using a Monte Carlo simulaïŋ―on approach. We are recognizing incremental stock-based compensaïŋ―on expense related to these amended awards for any of the remaining unvested tranches that are probable of achievement over the longer of the (a) esïŋ―mated implicit service period for performance-metric achievement, or (b) derived service period for market-based metric achievement. Stock-based compensaïŋ―on associated with a vesïŋ―ng tranche where vesïŋ―ng is no longer determined to be probable is reversed on a cumulaïŋ―ve basis and is no longer prospecïŋ―vely recognized in the period when such a determinaïŋ―on is made. We have esïŋ―mated remaining service periods for those tranches that have been deemed probable of achievement as of May 31, 2023 to be approximately one to two years. 

In connecïŋ―on with certain of our acquisiïŋ―ons, we assumed certain outstanding restricted stock-based awards and stock opïŋ―ons under each acquired companyâs respecïŋ―ve stock plans, or we subsïŋ―tuted substanïŋ―ally similar awards under the Plans. These restricted stock-based awards and stock opïŋ―ons assumed or subsïŋ―tuted generally retained

## **Employee Stock Purchase Plan** 

We have an Employee Stock Purchase Plan (Purchase Plan) that allows employees to purchase shares of common stock at a price per share that is 95% of the fair market value of Oracle stock as of the end of the semi-annual opïŋ―on period. As of May 31, 2023, 37 million shares were reserved for future issuances under the Purchase Plan. We issued approximately 2 million shares in each of fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021 under the Purchase Plan. 

## **Defined Contribuïŋ―on and Other Postreïŋ―rement Plans** 

We offer various defined contribuïŋ―on plans for our U.S. and non-U.S. employees. Total defined contribuïŋ―on plan expense was $470 million, $412 million and $380 million for fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely. 

In the U.S., regular employees can parïŋ―cipate in the Oracle Corporaïŋ―on 401(k) Savings and Investment Plan (Oracle 401(k) Plan). Parïŋ―cipants can generally contribute up to 40% of their eligible compensaïŋ―on on a per-pay-period basis as defined by the Oracle 401(k) Plan document or by the secïŋ―on 402(g) limit as defined by the U.S. Internal Revenue Service (IRS). We match a porïŋ―on of employee contribuïŋ―ons, currently 50% up to 6% of compensaïŋ―on each pay period, subject to maximum aggregate matching amounts. Our contribuïŋ―ons to the Oracle 401(k) Plan, net of forfeitures, were $198 million, $164 million and $150 million in fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021, respecïŋ―vely. 

We also offer non-qualified deferred compensaïŋ―on plans to certain employees whereby they may defer a porïŋ―on of their annual base and/or variable compensaïŋ―on unïŋ―l reïŋ―rement or a date specified by the employee in accordance with the plans. Deferred compensaïŋ―on plan assets and liabiliïŋ―es were each approximately $792 million and approximately $756 million as of May 31, 2023 and 2022, respecïŋ―vely, and were presented in other non-current assets and other non-current liabiliïŋ―es in the accompanying consolidated balance sheets.

Our effecïŋ―ve tax rates for each of the periods presented are the result of the mix of income and losses earned in various tax jurisdicïŋ―ons that apply a broad range of income tax rates. Our (provision for) benefit from income taxes varied from the tax computed at the U.S. federal statutory income tax rate for fiscal 2023, 2022 and 2021 primarily due to earnings in foreign operaïŋ―ons, state taxes, the U.S. research and development tax credit, seïŋ―lements with tax authoriïŋ―es, the tax effects of stock-based compensaïŋ―on, the Foreign Derived Intangible Income deducïŋ―on and the tax effect of Global Intangible Low-Taxed Income. In addiïŋ―on, for fiscal 2021, our benefit from income taxes varied from the tax computed at the U.S. federal statutory income tax rate primarily due to a total net deferred tax benefit of $2.3 billion as a result of a parïŋ―al realignment of our legal enïŋ―ty structure that resulted in the intra-group transfer of certain intellectual property rights.

Domesïŋ―cally, U.S. federal and state taxing authoriïŋ―es are currently examining income tax returns of Oracle and various acquired enïŋ―ïŋ―es for years through fiscal 2021. Many issues are at an advanced stage in the examinaïŋ―on process, the most significant of which include issues related to transfer pricing, domesïŋ―c producïŋ―on acïŋ―vity, one-ïŋ―me transiïŋ―on tax, foreign tax credits, research and development credits and state economic nexus. Our U.S. federal income tax returns have been examined for all years prior to fiscal 2013 and, with some excepïŋ―ons, we are no longer subject to audit for those periods. Our U.S. state income tax returns, with some excepïŋ―ons, have been examined for all years prior to fiscal 2007, and we are no longer subject to audit for those periods. 

Internaïŋ―onally, tax authoriïŋ―es for numerous non-U.S. jurisdicïŋ―ons are also examining or have examined returns of Oracle and various acquired enïŋ―ïŋ―es for years through fiscal 2023. Many of the relevant tax years are at an advanced stage in examinaïŋ―on or subsequent controversy resoluïŋ―on processes, the most significant of which include issues related to transfer pricing and withholding tax. The manner in which those issues are resolved and the ïŋ―ming thereof could potenïŋ―ally result in a range of decreases or increases in our unrecognized tax benefits over the next 12 months. We believe it was reasonably possible that, as of May 31, 2023, the gross unrecognized tax benefits could decrease (whether by payment, release, or a combinaïŋ―on of both) in the next 12 months by as much as $767 million ($262 million net of offseïŋ―ng tax benefits). We also believe it was reasonably possible that, as of May 31, 2023, the gross unrecognized tax benefits could increase in the next 12 months by as much as $637 million ($111 million net of offseïŋ―ng US tax benefits). With some excepïŋ―ons, we are generally no longer subject to tax examinaïŋ―ons in non-U.S. jurisdicïŋ―ons for years prior to fiscal 2001. 

We are under audit by the IRS and various other domesïŋ―c and foreign tax authoriïŋ―es with regards to income tax and indirect tax maïŋ―ers and are involved in various challenges and liïŋ―gaïŋ―on in a number of countries, including, in parïŋ―cular, Australia, Brazil, Canada, Germany, India, Indonesia, Israel, Italy, Mexico, New Zealand, Pakistan, Saudi Arabia, South Korea and Spain, where the amounts under controversy are significant. In some, although not all, cases, we have reserved for potenïŋ―al adjustments to our provision for income taxes and accrual of indirect taxes that may result from examinaïŋ―ons by, or any negoïŋ―ated agreements with, these tax authoriïŋ―es or final outcomes in judicial proceedings, and we believe that the final outcome of these examinaïŋ―ons, agreements or judicial proceedings will not have a material effect on our results of operaïŋ―ons. If events occur which indicate payment of these amounts is unnecessary, the reversal of the liabiliïŋ―es would result in the recogniïŋ―on of benefits in the period we determine the liabiliïŋ―es are no longer necessary. If our esïŋ―mates of the federal, state, and foreign income tax liabiliïŋ―es and indirect tax liabiliïŋ―es are less than the ulïŋ―mate assessment, it could result in a further charge to expense. 

We believe that we have adequately provided under GAAP for outcomes related to our tax audits. However, there can be no assurances as to the possible outcomes or any related financial statement effect thereof. 

## **14. SEGMENT INFORMATION** 

ASC 280, _Segment Reporïŋ―ng_ , establishes standards for reporïŋ―ng informaïŋ―on about operaïŋ―ng segments. Operaïŋ―ng segments are defined as components of an enterprise about which separate financial informaïŋ―on is available that is evaluated regularly by the chief operaïŋ―ng decision maker, or decision-making group, in deciding how to allocate resources and in assessing performance. Our chief operaïŋ―ng decision makers (CODMs) are our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer and Chief Technology Officer. We are organized by line of business and geographically. While our CODMs evaluate results in a number of different ways, the line of business management structure is the primary basis for which the allocaïŋ―on of resources and financial results are assessed. The tabular informaïŋ―on below presents financial 

100 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

informaïŋ―on that is provided to our CODMs for their review and assists our CODMs with evaluaïŋ―ng the companyâs performance and allocaïŋ―ng company resources. 

We have three businessesâcloud and license, hardware and servicesâeach of which is comprised of a single operaïŋ―ng segment. All three of our businesses market and sell our offerings globally to businesses of many sizes, government agencies, educaïŋ―onal insïŋ―tuïŋ―ons and resellers with a worldwide sales force posiïŋ―oned to offer the combinaïŋ―ons that best meet customer needs. 

Our cloud and license business engages in the sale, markeïŋ―ng and delivery of our enterprise applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies through cloud and onpremise deployment models including our cloud services and license support offerings; and our cloud license and on-premise license offerings. Cloud services and license support revenues are generated from offerings that are typically contracted with customers directly, billed to customers in advance, delivered to customers over ïŋ―me with our revenue recogniïŋ―on occurring over the contractual terms, and renewed by customers upon compleïŋ―on of the contractual terms. Cloud services and license support contracts provide customers with access to the latest updates to the applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies as they become available and for which the customer contracted and also include related technical support services over the contractual term. Cloud license and onpremise license revenues represent fees earned from granïŋ―ng customers licenses, generally on a perpetual basis, to use our database and middleware and our applicaïŋ―ons soïŋ―ware products within cloud and on-premise IT environments. We generally recognize revenues at the point in ïŋ―me the soïŋ―ware is made available to the customer to download and use, which typically is immediate upon signature of the license contract. In each fiscal year, our cloud and license businessâ contractual acïŋ―viïŋ―es are typically highest in our fourth fiscal quarter and the related cash flows are typically highest in the following quarter (i.e., in the first fiscal quarter of the next fiscal year) as we receive payments from these contracts. 

Our hardware business provides infrastructure technologies including Oracle Engineered Systems, servers, storage, industry-specific hardware, operaïŋ―ng systems, virtualizaïŋ―on, management and other hardware-related soïŋ―ware to support diverse IT environments. Our hardware business also offers hardware support, which provides customers with soïŋ―ware updates for the soïŋ―ware components that are essenïŋ―al to the funcïŋ―onality of their hardware products and can also include product repairs, maintenance services and technical support services that are typically delivered and recognized ratably over the contractual term. 

Our services business provides services to customers and partners to help maximize the performance of their investments in Oracle applicaïŋ―ons and infrastructure technologies. 

We do not track our assets for each business. Consequently, it is not pracïŋ―cal to show assets by operaïŋ―ng segment.
