## **16. LEGAL PROCEEDINGS** 

## **Derivaïŋ―ve Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on Concerning Oracleâs NetSuite Acquisiïŋ―on** 

On May 3 and July 18, 2017, two alleged stockholders filed separate derivaïŋ―ve lawsuits in the Court of Chancery of the State of Delaware, purportedly on Oracleâs behalf. Thereaïŋ―er, the court consolidated the two derivaïŋ―ve cases and designated the July 18, 2017 complaint as the operaïŋ―ve complaint. The consolidated lawsuit was brought against all the then-current members and one former member of our Board of Directors, and Oracle as a nominal defendant. 

104 

Table of Contents 

Index to Financial Statements 

Plainïŋ―ff alleged that the defendants breached their fiduciary duïŋ―es by causing Oracle to agree to purchase NetSuite Inc. (NetSuite) at an excessive price. The complaint sought (and the operaïŋ―ve complaint conïŋ―nues to seek) declaratory relief, unspecified monetary damages (including interest), and aïŋ―orneysâ fees and costs. The defendants filed a moïŋ―on to dismiss, which the court denied on March 19, 2018. 

On May 4, 2018, our Board of Directors established a Special Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on Commiïŋ―ee (SLC) to invesïŋ―gate the allegaïŋ―ons in this derivaïŋ―ve acïŋ―on. Three nonemployee directors served on the SLC. On August 15, 2019, the SLC filed a leïŋ―er with the court, staïŋ―ng that the SLC believed that plainïŋ―ff should be allowed to proceed with the derivaïŋ―ve liïŋ―gaïŋ―on on behalf of Oracle. Aïŋ―er the SLC advised the Board that it had fulfilled its duïŋ―es and obligaïŋ―ons, the Board withdrew the SLCâs authority, except that the SLC maintained certain authority to respond to discovery requests in the liïŋ―gaïŋ―on. 

Aïŋ―er plainïŋ―ff filed the July 18, 2017 complaint, an addiïŋ―onal plainïŋ―ff joined the case. Plainïŋ―ffs filed several amended complaints, and filed their most recent amended complaint on December 11, 2020. The operaïŋ―ve complaint asserts claims for breach of fiduciary duty against our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer, our Chief Technology Officer, the estate of Mark Hurd (our former Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer who passed away on October 18, 2019), and two other members of our Board of Directors. Oracle is named as a nominal defendant. On December 11, 2020, the estate of Mark Hurd and the two other members of our Board of Directors moved to dismiss this complaint. On June 21, 2021, the court granted this moïŋ―on as to the estate of Mark Hurd and one Board member and denied the moïŋ―on as to the other Board member, who filed an answer to the complaint on August 9, 2021. On December 28, 2020, our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer, our Chief Technology Officer, and Oracle as a nominal defendant filed answers to the operaïŋ―ve complaint. 

Trial commenced on July 18, 2022, and has concluded. On November 18, 2022, the court held a final hearing on the parïŋ―esâ post-trial briefing. On December 27, 2022, the court âso orderedâ a sïŋ―pulaïŋ―on, dismissing the Board member from this acïŋ―on. On May 12, 2023, the court issued its trial ruling, finding for defendants and rejecïŋ―ng plainïŋ―ffsâ claims. On May 22, 2023, plainïŋ―ffs filed a moïŋ―on for aïŋ―orneysâ fees, claiming that this lawsuit had conferred a benefit on Oracle. On May 31, 2023, defendants filed a bill of costs, as the prevailing party. 

While Oracle conïŋ―nues to evaluate these claims, we do not believe this liïŋ―gaïŋ―on will have a material impact on our financial posiïŋ―on or results of operaïŋ―ons. 

## **Derivaïŋ―ve Liïŋ―gaïŋ―on Concerning Oracleâs Cloud Business** 

On February 12 and May 6, 2019, two stockholder derivaïŋ―ve lawsuits were filed in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California. The cases were consolidated, and on July 8, 2019, a single plainïŋ―ff filed a consolidated complaint. The consolidated complaint brought various claims relaïŋ―ng to a Rule 10b-5 class acïŋ―on that was filed in the same court on August 10, 2018, and which was seïŋ―led for a payment by the Company of $17,500,000. That maïŋ―er is now concluded. In the Rule 10b-5 class acïŋ―on, plainïŋ―ff alleged Oracle and certain Oracle officers made or were responsible for false and misleading statements regarding Oracleâs cloud business. 

Plainïŋ―ff in the derivaïŋ―ve acïŋ―on filed an amended complaint on June 4, 2021. The derivaïŋ―ve suit is brought by an alleged stockholder of Oracle, purportedly on Oracleâs behalf, against our Chief Technology Officer, our Chief Execuïŋ―ve Officer, and the estate of Mark Hurd. Plainïŋ―ff claims that the alleged acïŋ―ons described in the 10b-5 class acïŋ―on caused harm to Oracle, including harming Oracle because Oracle allegedly repurchased its own stock at an inflated price. Plainïŋ―ff also claims that defendants violated their fiduciary duïŋ―es of candor, good faith, loyalty, and due care by failing to prevent this alleged harm. Plainïŋ―ff also brings derivaïŋ―ve claims for violaïŋ―ons of federal securiïŋ―es laws. Plainïŋ―ff seeks a ruling that this case may proceed as a derivaïŋ―ve acïŋ―on, a finding that defendants are liable for breaching their fiduciary duïŋ―es, an award of damages to Oracle, an order direcïŋ―ng defendants to enact corporate reforms, aïŋ―orneysâ fees and costs, and unspecified relief. On June 14, 2021, the court âso orderedâ a sïŋ―pulaïŋ―on from the parïŋ―es, staying this case pending resoluïŋ―on of the 10b-5 acïŋ―on, and the court âso orderedâ two addiïŋ―onal sïŋ―pulaïŋ―ons, staying the case unïŋ―l January 31, 2023. Defendants are scheduled to file their moïŋ―on to dismiss by June 29, 2023. 

While Oracle conïŋ―nues to evaluate these claims, we do not believe these maïŋ―ers will have a material impact on our financial posiïŋ―on or results of operaïŋ―ons.
